- The recommendations are specific and actionable, which can drive improvements in future setups.

### Issues Found
**CRITICAL:**
- None

**MAJOR:**
- The document could benefit from a clearer summary of the most critical improvements needed, as it currently presents a lot of information that might overwhelm the reader.

**MINOR:**
- Some sections could be more concise to improve readability.
- The use of technical jargon might be challenging for non-technical readers.

### Specific Recommendations
1. **Executive Summary**: The summary could be more concise, focusing on the top 3-5 key findings and recommendations to provide a quick overview.
2. **Agent Experience Analysis**: Consider breaking down the "What Was Difficult" section into bullet points for each problem to enhance readability.

### Missing Elements

- Consider including a section on potential risks if the recommendations are not implemented.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 16-20 hours (higher than planned due to missing complexity)

## Strengths
- Excellent problem identification and user experience focus
- Clear objective with measurable success metrics (3 hours → 5 minutes)
- Well-structured interactive questionnaire approach
- Comprehensive template system design
- Good security considerations for API key handling
- Thorough acceptance criteria and test plan
- Realistic timeline estimation for core features

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] **CLI Integration Conflict**: Plan proposes `adversarial agent-setup` command but existing CLI uses `adversarial-workflow` package structure. The command should be `adversarial-workflow agent-setup` or needs setup.py entry point clarification.
- [CRITICAL] **Existing Code Duplication**: The plan recreates functionality that already exists in `cli.py` (init_interactive, create_env_file_interactive, render_template). Need to refactor existing code rather than duplicate.
- [CRITICAL] **Template Location Mismatch**: Plan puts templates in `adversarial_workflow/templates/agent-context/` but existing templates are in `adversarial_workflow/templates/`. This breaks existing template discovery.
- [MEDIUM] **Migration Logic Underspecified**: The tasks/ → delegation/tasks/ migration is mentioned but not detailed. This is a high-risk data operation.
- [MEDIUM] **Rollback Complexity**: Plan mentions rollback on critical failures but doesn't specify what constitutes "critical" or how rollback works.
- [LOW] **Progress Indicators**: Colored output and progress bars add complexity without clear user value for a 5-minute operation.

## Missing or Unclear
- **Integration with Existing Init**: How does this relate to the existing `adversarial-workflow init` command? Should it replace it, extend it, or coexist?
- **Template Variable Context**: What variables need to be available for template rendering? The plan mentions `{{PROJECT_NAME}}` but existing templates may need different variables.
- **Aider Integration**: How does the aider installation integrate with existing `.aider.conf.yml.template`?
- **Config File Interaction**: How does this interact with existing `.adversarial/config.yml` structure?
- **Backward Compatibility**: What happens to projects already using the current init system?

## Specific Recommendations
1. **Refactor, Don't Duplicate**: Extend existing `init_interactive()` function rather than creating parallel setup wizard. This reduces code duplication and maintains consistency.
2. **Unified Command Structure**: Make this an enhancement to existing `adversarial-workflow init --interactive` rather than a separate command, or clearly specify the relationship.
3. **Template Consolidation**: Use existing template directory structure and extend existing templates rather than creating parallel template system.
4. **Migration Safety**: Add detailed migration plan with backup/restore capability for tasks/ directory operations.
5. **Incremental Implementation**: Start with core functionality (directory setup, template rendering) before adding advanced features (aider installation, API key management).

## Questions for Plan Author
1. **Command Relationship**: Should this replace the existing `init` command, extend it with a `--wizard` flag, or be a separate command? What's the migration path for existing users?
2. **Code Reuse Strategy**: The existing `cli.py` has 400+ lines including similar functionality. How do we avoid duplication while maintaining the improved UX?
3. **Template Compatibility**: Existing templates use different variable patterns. Should we standardize on one approach or support both?
4. **Scope Creep**: The plan includes aider installation and API key management. Are these essential for the core "setup wizard" goal, or could they be separate features?

## Approval Conditions
**For NEEDS_REVISION approval, address these specific issues:**

1. **Clarify CLI Integration**: 
   - Specify exact command name and entry point
   - Define relationship to existing `init` command
   - Update setup.py entry point specification

2. **Refactor Existing Code**:
   - Audit existing `cli.py` functions for reuse opportunities
   - Plan how to extend rather than duplicate functionality
   - Specify which existing functions will be modified vs. new

3. **Template Strategy**:
   - Use existing `adversarial_workflow/templates/` directory
   - Specify how new templates integrate with existing ones
   - Define template variable standardization approach

4. **Migration Safety Plan**:
   - Detail the tasks/ → delegation/tasks/ migration process
   - Specify backup/rollback procedures
   - Define what constitutes a "safe" migration

5. **Reduce Initial Scope**:
   - Consider making aider installation and API key setup optional Phase 2 features
   - Focus initial implementation on core directory setup and template rendering
   - Add complexity incrementally after core functionality works

**Once these issues are addressed, the plan should be ready for implementation.**

"""
Setup file for adversarial-workflow package.
Uses pyproject.toml for configuration (PEP 621).
"""

from setuptools import setup

# Configuration is in pyproject.toml
setup(
    entry_points={
        'console_scripts': [
            'adversarial-workflow=adversarial_workflow.cli:main',
            'agent-setup=adversarial_workflow.cli:agent_setup_main',
        ],
    }
)

adversarial_workflow/cli.py

<<<<<<< SEARCH
def main():
    """Main CLI entry point."""
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description="Adversarial Workflow - Multi-stage AI code review",
        formatter_class=argparse.RawDescriptionHelpFormatter,
        epilog="""
Examples:
  adversarial init                      # Initialize in current project
  adversarial init --interactive        # Interactive setup wizard
  adversarial quickstart                # Quick start with example
  adversarial check                     # Validate setup
  adversarial evaluate tasks/feat.md    # Evaluate plan
  adversarial review                    # Review implementation
  adversarial validate "npm test"       # Validate with tests

For more information: https://github.com/movito/adversarial-workflow
        """,
    )

    parser.add_argument(
        "--version", action="version", version=f"adversarial-workflow {__version__}"
    )

    subparsers = parser.add_subparsers(dest="command", help="Command to run")

    # init command
    init_parser = subparsers.add_parser("init", help="Initialize workflow in project")
    init_parser.add_argument(
        "--path", default=".", help="Project path (default: current directory)"
    )
    init_parser.add_argument(
        "--interactive", "-i", action="store_true", help="Interactive setup wizard"
    )

    # quickstart command
    subparsers.add_parser(
        "quickstart", help="Quick start with example task (recommended for new users)"
    )

    # check command (with doctor alias)
    subparsers.add_parser("check", help="Validate setup and dependencies")
    subparsers.add_parser("doctor", help="Alias for 'check'")

    # evaluate command
    eval_parser = subparsers.add_parser("evaluate", help="Run Phase 1: Plan evaluation")
    eval_parser.add_argument("task_file", help="Task file to evaluate")

    # review command
    subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")

    # validate command
    validate_parser = subparsers.add_parser(
        "validate", help="Run Phase 4: Test validation"
    )
    validate_parser.add_argument(
        "test_command", nargs="?", help="Test command to run (optional)"
    )

    args = parser.parse_args()

    if not args.command:
        parser.print_help()
        return 0

    # Execute command
    if args.command == "init":
        if args.interactive:
            return init_interactive(args.path)
        else:
            return init(args.path)
    elif args.command == "quickstart":
        return quickstart()
    elif args.command in ["check", "doctor"]:
        return check()
    elif args.command == "evaluate":
        return evaluate(args.task_file)
    elif args.command == "review":
        return review()
    elif args.command == "validate":
        return validate(args.test_command)
    else:
        parser.print_help()
        return 1
=======
def agent_setup() -> int:
    """Interactive setup wizard for agent coordination system."""
    
    # Check platform compatibility first
    if not check_platform_compatibility():
        return 1

    print(f"\n{BOLD}{CYAN}🤖 Agent Coordination System Setup{RESET}")
    print()
    print("This wizard will set up the full agent coordination system with:")
    print("  • Agent handoff configuration")
    print("  • Task delegation structure") 
    print("  • Session logging")
    print("  • Integration with adversarial workflow")
    print()

    # Pre-flight discovery
    print(f"{BOLD}Scanning project structure...{RESET}")
    
    existing_agent_context = os.path.exists(".agent-context")
    existing_delegation = os.path.exists("delegation")
    existing_tasks = os.path.exists("tasks")
    existing_adversarial = os.path.exists(".adversarial")
    
    print(f"  {'✓' if existing_agent_context else '○'} .agent-context/ directory")
    print(f"  {'✓' if existing_delegation else '○'} delegation/ directory")
    print(f"  {'✓' if existing_tasks else '○'} tasks/ directory")
    print(f"  {'✓' if existing_adversarial else '○'} .adversarial/ configuration")
    print()

    # Interactive questionnaire (4 questions max)
    print_box(
        "Configuration Questions",
        [
            "Please answer a few questions to customize your setup:",
        ],
    )

    # Q1: Use delegation/tasks/ structure?
    use_delegation = prompt_user("Use delegation/tasks/ structure? (recommended for agent coordination)", default="Y")
    use_delegation = use_delegation.lower() in ["y", "yes", ""]

    # Q2: Organize root docs into docs/?
    organize_docs = prompt_user("Organize root documentation into docs/ directory?", default="Y")
    organize_docs = organize_docs.lower() in ["y", "yes", ""]

    # Q3: Install aider-chat if missing?
    install_aider = True
    if not shutil.which("aider"):
        install_aider = prompt_user("Install aider-chat? (required for agent workflows)", default="Y")
        install_aider = install_aider.lower() in ["y", "yes", ""]

    # Q4: Configure API keys now?
    configure_keys = prompt_user("Configure API keys now?", default="n")
    configure_keys = configure_keys.lower() in ["y", "yes"]

    print()
    print(f"{BOLD}Setting up agent coordination system...{RESET}")

    # Create directory structure
    if use_delegation:
        os.makedirs("delegation/tasks/active", exist_ok=True)
        os.makedirs("delegation/tasks/completed", exist_ok=True)
        os.makedirs("delegation/tasks/analysis", exist_ok=True)
        print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Created delegation/tasks/ structure")
        
        # Migrate existing tasks if they exist
        if existing_tasks and not existing_delegation:
            migrate = prompt_user("Migrate existing tasks/ to delegation/tasks/?", default="Y")
            if migrate.lower() in ["y", "yes", ""]:
                try:
                    shutil.move("tasks", "delegation/tasks/active")
                    print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Migrated tasks/ to delegation/tasks/active/")
                except Exception as e:
                    print(f"{YELLOW}⚠️{RESET} Migration failed: {e}")

    # Organize documentation
    if organize_docs:
        docs_files = [f for f in os.listdir(".") if f.endswith((".md", ".txt", ".rst")) and f not in ["README.md", "CHANGELOG.md", "LICENSE"]]
        if docs_files:
            os.makedirs("docs", exist_ok=True)
            moved_count = 0
            for doc_file in docs_files:
                try:
                    shutil.move(doc_file, f"docs/{doc_file}")
                    moved_count += 1
                except Exception:
                    pass
            if moved_count > 0:
                print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Organized {moved_count} documentation files into docs/")

    # Install aider if requested and missing
    if install_aider and not shutil.which("aider"):
        print("Installing aider-chat...")
        try:
            subprocess.run([sys.executable, "-m", "pip", "install", "aider-chat"], check=True, capture_output=True)
            print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Installed aider-chat")
        except subprocess.CalledProcessError:
            print(f"{YELLOW}⚠️{RESET} Failed to install aider-chat automatically")
            print("   Please install manually: pip install aider-chat")

    # Initialize .agent-context with templates
    os.makedirs(".agent-context", exist_ok=True)
    os.makedirs(".agent-context/session-logs", exist_ok=True)

    # Create template context
    project_name = os.path.basename(os.path.abspath("."))
    template_context = {
        "PROJECT_NAME": project_name,
        "DATE": "2025-10-16",  # Current date
        "PYTHON_VERSION": f"{sys.version_info.major}.{sys.version_info.minor}",
    }

    # Create agent-handoffs.json
    agent_handoffs = {
        "agents": {
            "coordinator": {
                "role": "Task coordination and delegation",
                "model": "claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
                "handoff_triggers": ["task_assignment", "status_update", "conflict_resolution"]
            },
            "feature-developer": {
                "role": "Feature implementation and development",
                "model": "claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022", 
                "handoff_triggers": ["implementation_request", "code_review_response"]
            },
            "code-reviewer": {
                "role": "Code quality and security review",
                "model": "gpt-4o",
                "handoff_triggers": ["review_request", "security_audit"]
            },
            "test-runner": {
                "role": "Test execution and validation",
                "model": "gpt-4o",
                "handoff_triggers": ["test_request", "validation_needed"]
            },
            "document-reviewer": {
                "role": "Documentation review and improvement",
                "model": "claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
                "handoff_triggers": ["doc_review", "clarity_check"]
            },
            "security-reviewer": {
                "role": "Security analysis and vulnerability assessment",
                "model": "gpt-4o",
                "handoff_triggers": ["security_review", "vulnerability_scan"]
            },
            "api-developer": {
                "role": "API design and implementation",
                "model": "claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022",
                "handoff_triggers": ["api_design", "endpoint_implementation"]
            }
        },
        "project_context": {
            "name": project_name,
            "setup_date": template_context["DATE"],
            "python_version": template_context["PYTHON_VERSION"]
        }
    }

    with open(".agent-context/agent-handoffs.json", "w") as f:
        import json
        json.dump(agent_handoffs, f, indent=2)
    print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Created .agent-context/agent-handoffs.json")

    # Create current-state.json
    current_state = {
        "current_phase": "setup",
        "active_tasks": [],
        "completed_tasks": [],
        "pending_reviews": [],
        "last_updated": template_context["DATE"],
        "project_status": "initialized"
    }

    with open(".agent-context/current-state.json", "w") as f:
        json.dump(current_state, f, indent=2)
    print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Created .agent-context/current-state.json")

    # Create README.md for agent context
    readme_content = f"""# Agent Context for {project_name}

This directory contains the agent coordination system configuration.

## Files

- `agent-handoffs.json` - Agent roles and handoff triggers
- `current-state.json` - Current project state and active tasks
- `session-logs/` - Agent session logs and interactions

## Usage

The agent coordination system integrates with the adversarial workflow to provide:

1. **Task Delegation** - Automatic routing of tasks to appropriate agents
2. **Context Preservation** - Maintains state across agent handoffs  
3. **Session Logging** - Tracks all agent interactions
4. **Quality Assurance** - Multi-agent review process

## Setup Date
{template_context["DATE"]}

## Python Version  
{template_context["PYTHON_VERSION"]}
"""

    with open(".agent-context/README.md", "w") as f:
        f.write(readme_content)
    print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Created .agent-context/README.md")

    # Configure API keys if requested
    if configure_keys:
        create_env_file_interactive(".")

    # Initialize adversarial workflow if not already done
    if not existing_adversarial:
        print()
        print("Initializing adversarial workflow integration...")
        result = init(".", interactive=False)
        if result == 0:
            print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Initialized adversarial workflow")

    # Update .gitignore
    gitignore_entries = [
        ".agent-context/session-logs/",
        ".env",
    ]
    
    gitignore_path = ".gitignore"
    if os.path.exists(gitignore_path):
        with open(gitignore_path, "r") as f:
            existing = f.read()
    else:
        existing = ""

    with open(gitignore_path, "a") as f:
        if "# Agent Coordination System" not in existing:
            f.write("\n# Agent Coordination System\n")
            for entry in gitignore_entries:
                if entry not in existing:
                    f.write(f"{entry}\n")
    print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} Updated .gitignore")

    # Verification
    print()
    print(f"{BOLD}Verifying setup...{RESET}")
    
    # Validate JSON files
    try:
        with open(".agent-context/agent-handoffs.json", "r") as f:
            json.load(f)
        print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} agent-handoffs.json is valid")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"{RED}❌{RESET} agent-handoffs.json validation failed: {e}")

    try:
        with open(".agent-context/current-state.json", "r") as f:
            json.load(f)
        print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} current-state.json is valid")
    except Exception as e:
        print(f"{RED}❌{RESET} current-state.json validation failed: {e}")

    # Check agent count
    agent_count = len(agent_handoffs["agents"])
    if agent_count == 7:
        print(f"{GREEN}✅{RESET} All 7 agents initialized")
    else:
        print(f"{YELLOW}⚠️{RESET} Expected 7 agents, found {agent_count}")

    # Success message
    print_box(
        f"{GREEN}✅ Agent Coordination System Setup Complete!{RESET}",
        [
            "Created:",
            "  ✓ .agent-context/ (agent configuration)",
            "  ✓ agent-handoffs.json (7 agents configured)",
            "  ✓ current-state.json (project state tracking)",
            "  ✓ session-logs/ (for agent interactions)",
            f"  ✓ {'delegation/tasks/' if use_delegation else 'tasks/'} (task structure)",
            "  ✓ Integration with adversarial workflow",
            "",
            "Your agent coordination system is ready!",
            "",
            "Next steps:",
            "  1. Create your first task in delegation/tasks/active/",
            "  2. Use agent handoff triggers in task descriptions",
            "  3. Run: adversarial-workflow evaluate <task-file>",
            "",
            "Agent roles configured:",
            "  • coordinator - Task delegation and management",
            "  • feature-developer - Implementation work", 
            "  • code-reviewer - Quality assurance",
            "  • test-runner - Test execution",
            "  • document-reviewer - Documentation",
            "  • security-reviewer - Security analysis",
            "  • api-developer - API design",
            "",
            "Learn more: .agent-context/README.md",
        ],
    )

    return 0


def agent_setup_main():
    """Entry point for standalone agent-setup command."""
    sys.exit(agent_setup())


def main():
    """Main CLI entry point."""
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description="Adversarial Workflow - Multi-stage AI code review",
        formatter_class=argparse.RawDescriptionHelpFormatter,
        epilog="""
Examples:
  adversarial-workflow init                      # Initialize in current project
  adversarial-workflow init --interactive        # Interactive setup wizard
  adversarial-workflow quickstart                # Quick start with example
  adversarial-workflow check                     # Validate setup
  adversarial-workflow evaluate tasks/feat.md    # Evaluate plan
  adversarial-workflow review                    # Review implementation
  adversarial-workflow validate "npm test"       # Validate with tests
  
  agent-setup                                    # Setup agent coordination system

For more information: https://github.com/movito/adversarial-workflow
        """,
    )

    parser.add_argument(
        "--version", action="version", version=f"adversarial-workflow {__version__}"
    )

    subparsers = parser.add_subparsers(dest="command", help="Command to run")

    # init command
    init_parser = subparsers.add_parser("init", help="Initialize workflow in project")
    init_parser.add_argument(
        "--path", default=".", help="Project path (default: current directory)"
    )
    init_parser.add_argument(
        "--interactive", "-i", action="store_true", help="Interactive setup wizard"
    )

    # agent-setup command
    subparsers.add_parser(
        "agent-setup", help="Interactive setup wizard for agent coordination system"
    )

    # quickstart command
    subparsers.add_parser(
        "quickstart", help="Quick start with example task (recommended for new users)"
    )

    # check command (with doctor alias)
    subparsers.add_parser("check", help="Validate setup and dependencies")
    subparsers.add_parser("doctor", help="Alias for 'check'")

    # evaluate command
    eval_parser = subparsers.add_parser("evaluate", help="Run Phase 1: Plan evaluation")
    eval_parser.add_argument("task_file", help="Task file to evaluate")

    # review command
    subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")

    # validate command
    validate_parser = subparsers.add_parser(
        "validate", help="Run Phase 4: Test validation"
    )
    validate_parser.add_argument(
        "test_command", nargs="?", help="Test command to run (optional)"
    )

    args = parser.parse_args()

    if not args.command:
        parser.print_help()
        return 0

    # Execute command
    if args.command == "init":
        if args.interactive:
            return init_interactive(args.path)
        else:
            return init(args.path)
    elif args.command == "agent-setup":
        return agent_setup()
    elif args.command == "quickstart":
        return quickstart()
    elif args.command in ["check", "doctor"]:
        return check()
    elif args.command == "evaluate":
        return evaluate(args.task_file)
    elif args.command == "review":
        return review()
    elif args.command == "validate":
        return validate(args.test_command)
    else:
        parser.print_help()
        return 1

- Clear, well-structured dataclass design with appropriate field types

- Comprehensive test plan covering creation, defaults, types, and equality
- Proper module structure with clean exports
- Type hints compatible with Python 3.10+
- Implementation notes address key technical considerations
- Clear acceptance criteria that are measurable

## Concerns & Risks
- [LOW] The `aliases` field as `list[str]` could lead to mutation issues if shared between instances, though `field(default_factory=list)` correctly addresses this
- [LOW] No validation logic specified, but implementation notes correctly defer this to the parser task
- [MEDIUM] Missing explicit mention of `from __future__ import annotations` import in the code examples, though it's mentioned in implementation notes

## Missing or Unclear
- Test file location and naming convention could be more explicit (assumes `tests/` directory exists)
- No mention of whether existing project structure needs to be verified before creating new directories
- Import statement examples don't show the `from __future__ import annotations` that's mentioned in notes

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add the `from __future__ import annotations` import to the code examples in the dataclass definition
2. Consider adding a brief note about verifying the `tests/` directory structure exists
3. The test examples could include a test for the `field(default_factory=list)` behavior to ensure list fields aren't shared between instances

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Should there be any basic validation in the dataclass (e.g., non-empty strings) or is deferring all validation to the parser the right approach?
2. Are there any existing project conventions for test file organization that should be followed?
3. Should the `version` field follow semantic versioning constraints or remain a free-form string?

This plan is approved as-is. The minor improvements suggested above would enhance clarity but don't block implementation. The core design is sound, the scope is appropriate for a foundational task, and the testing approach is thorough. The implementation notes show good awareness of the broader architecture context.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 4-5 hours (slightly higher than estimated due to missing elements)

## Strengths
- Comprehensive YAML schema definition with clear required/optional fields
- Well-structured error handling with custom exception types
- Good separation of concerns (parsing vs discovery)
- Thorough test coverage plan covering edge cases
- Clear acceptance criteria and implementation notes
- Proper handling of aliases and conflict detection
- Security consideration using `yaml.safe_load()`

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing integration with existing CLI command registration system - how do discovered evaluators become actual CLI commands?
- [CRITICAL] No validation of `model` field values - should validate against supported models
- [CRITICAL] No validation of `api_key_env` - should check if it's a valid environment variable name
- [MEDIUM] Warning system uses both `warnings.warn()` and `print()` inconsistently
- [MEDIUM] No caching mechanism for discovery - will re-parse YAML files on every discovery call
- [MEDIUM] No handling of circular dependencies or duplicate names across different sources
- [LOW] Missing logging integration for better debugging

## Missing or Unclear
- How discovered evaluators integrate with the CLI command system (registration mechanism)
- Validation rules for model names and API key environment variable names
- Error handling strategy when environment variables are missing at runtime
- Performance considerations for large numbers of evaluator files
- Interaction with built-in evaluators (precedence rules)
- Migration path for existing evaluator configurations

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add model validation against a known list of supported models
2. Add environment variable name validation (valid identifier format)
3. Implement caching for parsed evaluators to avoid re-parsing on every discovery
4. Standardize warning/error reporting (use logging module consistently)
5. Add integration points showing how discovered evaluators become CLI commands
6. Consider adding a `validate_evaluator_config()` function for runtime validation

## Questions for Plan Author
1. How do discovered evaluators get registered as CLI commands? Is there a separate registration step?
2. What happens when a required environment variable is missing at evaluation time?
3. Should there be precedence rules between local evaluators and built-in ones?
4. How should the system handle evaluator name conflicts between different YAML files?
5. Is there a maximum number of evaluators that should be supported?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following must be addressed:

1. **Add CLI Integration Section**: Specify how `EvaluatorConfig` objects become actual CLI commands
2. **Add Validation Functions**: Include validation for model names and environment variable names
3. **Clarify Error Handling**: Standardize on logging vs warnings vs print statements
4. **Add Runtime Validation**: Specify how/when environment variables are validated
5. **Define Integration Points**: Show how this connects to the broader plugin architecture
6. **Add Performance Considerations**: Address caching and scalability concerns

The core design is sound, but these integration and validation gaps need to be filled before implementation to avoid rework and ensure the feature works end-to-end.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 4-5 hours (slightly higher than estimated due to missing elements)

## Strengths
- Comprehensive YAML schema definition with clear required/optional fields
- Well-structured separation of concerns (parsing vs discovery)
- Robust error handling with custom exception types
- Thorough validation including name format validation with regex
- Good conflict resolution strategy (first-wins policy with logging)
- Detailed test cases covering edge cases and error conditions
- Clear module structure and exports
- Performance considerations noted
- Security consideration (yaml.safe_load)

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing integration with existing codebase - no mention of how this connects to current evaluator system
- [CRITICAL] Inconsistent logging approach - uses both `logging` and `warnings.warn` in different places
- [MEDIUM] No validation of YAML file encoding/format beyond syntax
- [MEDIUM] Alias validation is incomplete - doesn't check if aliases follow same naming rules as primary names
- [MEDIUM] No consideration of YAML file size limits or malicious content
- [LOW] Discovery function could be more efficient by caching results
- [LOW] No mention of handling symbolic links in evaluator directory

## Missing or Unclear
- How does this integrate with existing evaluator loading mechanisms?
- What happens to built-in evaluators vs local evaluators - precedence rules?
- No specification for handling duplicate filenames (e.g., `test.yml` and `test.yaml`)
- Missing error recovery strategies when partial discovery fails
- No mention of configuration validation beyond required fields (e.g., reasonable prompt length)
- Unclear how this fits with the broader plugin architecture mentioned in parent epic
- No specification for handling nested directories or subdirectories in evaluators folder

## Specific Recommendations
1. **Standardize logging approach** - Remove `warnings.warn` usage and use `logging` consistently throughout
2. **Add alias name validation** - Apply same regex validation to aliases as primary names
3. **Specify integration points** - Document how this connects to existing evaluator system
4. **Add file extension handling** - Support both `.yml` and `.yaml` extensions with clear precedence
5. **Add configuration validation** - Basic sanity checks (prompt not empty, reasonable field lengths)
6. **Consider caching mechanism** - For performance if discovery is called frequently
7. **Add encoding specification** - Explicitly handle UTF-8 encoding for YAML files

## Questions for Plan Author
1. How does this discovery mechanism integrate with any existing evaluator loading system?
2. Should aliases be subject to the same naming validation as primary evaluator names?
3. What's the expected behavior if both `evaluator.yml` and `evaluator.yaml` exist?
4. Should there be any validation on the content/format of prompts beyond "not empty"?
5. How does this fit with the broader plugin architecture - are there other discovery mechanisms planned?

## Approval Conditions
**For NEEDS_REVISION approval, address these specific issues:**

1. **Fix logging inconsistency**: Remove `warnings.warn` from parser, use `logging.getLogger(__name__).warning()` consistently
2. **Add alias validation**: Apply name format validation to all aliases, not just primary names
3. **Specify integration approach**: Add a section explaining how this connects to existing evaluator systems
4. **Handle both .yml and .yaml**: Specify behavior when both extensions exist (suggest .yml takes precedence)
5. **Add basic content validation**: Check that prompts are non-empty strings and reasonable length
6. **Clarify scope boundaries**: Make explicit what validation is deferred to runtime vs handled here

The core design is sound and the implementation approach is well-thought-out. These revisions will make the plan more robust and implementable without major architectural changes.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 4-5 hours (slightly over estimate due to missing pieces)

## Strengths
- Excellent scope clarification that clearly delineates what this task does vs. dependent tasks
- Comprehensive YAML schema with good balance of required vs. optional fields
- Thorough validation logic including name format validation and alias handling
- Well-structured error handling with custom exception types
- Good separation of concerns between parsing and discovery
- Detailed test cases covering edge cases and error conditions
- Clear logging strategy using Python's logging module
- Performance considerations noted
- Good integration points with dependent tasks clearly identified

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing import statements in discovery.py implementation (yaml, logging, re, Path)
- [CRITICAL] Test file structure and imports not specified - unclear how tests integrate with existing test suite
- [MEDIUM] No specification of logging configuration or log levels for different scenarios
- [MEDIUM] UTF-8 encoding assumption not enforced in code (could fail on non-UTF-8 files)
- [MEDIUM] No handling of circular alias references (alias pointing to another alias)
- [LOW] Regex pattern could be more restrictive (currently allows consecutive hyphens/underscores)
- [LOW] No mention of YAML file size limits or performance with large files

## Missing or Unclear
- Import statements missing from the discovery.py implementation code blocks
- Test runner integration (pytest configuration, test discovery)
- Logging configuration setup (where/how logging is configured)
- Error message formatting consistency across different error types
- Handling of YAML files with BOM or different encodings
- Behavior when .adversarial directory exists but evaluators subdirectory doesn't
- Integration testing approach (how to test the full discovery pipeline)

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add all required import statements to the discovery.py implementation
2. Specify test file location and pytest integration approach
3. Add explicit UTF-8 encoding to file reading: `yml_file.read_text(encoding='utf-8')`
4. Consider adding a check for circular alias references
5. Add logging level specifications (INFO for successful discovery, WARNING for skipped files)
6. Consider making the regex pattern more restrictive: `r'^[a-zA-Z][a-zA-Z0-9]*(?:[_-][a-zA-Z0-9]+)*$'`
7. Add error handling for file permission issues and encoding errors

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Should the discovery function handle symbolic links in the evaluators directory?
2. What's the expected behavior if a YAML file is valid but the referenced model doesn't exist?
3. Should there be a maximum file size limit for YAML files to prevent memory issues?
4. How should the system handle YAML files that are being written to during discovery?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following changes are needed:

1. **Add missing imports** to the discovery.py implementation code blocks
2. **Specify test integration** - clarify where tests go and how they run
3. **Add UTF-8 encoding** explicitly to file reading operations
4. **Clarify logging setup** - where/how logging is configured for this module
5. **Add error handling** for file encoding issues and permission errors

The core design is sound and the implementation approach is well thought out. These are primarily completeness issues rather than fundamental design flaws.

## Strengths
- Excellent scope clarification that clearly delineates what this task does vs. dependent tasks
- Comprehensive YAML schema with good balance of required/optional fields
- Thorough validation logic including name format validation and alias handling
- Well-structured error handling with custom exception types
- Detailed test plan covering edge cases and error conditions
- Good separation of concerns between parsing and discovery
- Clear integration points with other tasks (ADV-0015, ADV-0017, ADV-0018)
- Thoughtful design decisions (UTF-8 encoding, .yml only, flat directory structure)

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing import statements in discovery.py implementation - `yaml` and `re` imports are used but not shown in the main implementation block
- [CRITICAL] Test file location and structure not clearly specified - mentions "standard pytest location" but doesn't show the actual test structure
- [MEDIUM] No explicit handling of circular alias references (alias pointing to another alias)
- [MEDIUM] Logging configuration dependency not clearly addressed - mentions CLI handles it but no fallback if logging not configured
- [MEDIUM] File encoding error handling not specified - what happens if file isn't UTF-8?
- [LOW] Performance note mentions 10-50ms but no basis provided for this estimate
- [LOW] Symbolic link behavior mentioned but not tested

## Missing or Unclear
- Import statements missing from the main implementation blocks
- No specification of how to handle YAML files with BOM (Byte Order Mark)
- No clear specification of what constitutes "empty" YAML (None vs empty dict vs whitespace-only)
- Test file structure and pytest configuration not detailed
- No mention of how to handle very large YAML files or memory constraints
- Integration testing with actual CLI not addressed (only unit tests specified)

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add explicit import statements to all code blocks in the implementation section
2. Specify complete test file structure including imports and pytest fixtures
3. Add handling for file encoding errors with graceful fallback
4. Consider adding a simple integration test that verifies discovery works end-to-end
5. Add validation to prevent circular alias references
6. Specify behavior for edge cases like YAML files with only comments
7. Add logging fallback configuration for when module is used outside CLI context

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Should the parser handle YAML files with multiple documents (using `---` separators)?
2. How should the system behave if an evaluator YAML file is modified while the application is running?
3. Should there be any caching mechanism for discovered evaluators, or is re-parsing on each discovery acceptable?
4. What's the expected behavior if a YAML file contains valid YAML but invalid UTF-8 sequences?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following changes are needed:

1. **Add missing imports**: Include all necessary import statements in the implementation code blocks
2. **Complete test specification**: Show the full test file structure with proper imports and any needed fixtures
3. **Add encoding error handling**: Specify how to handle non-UTF-8 files gracefully
4. **Clarify empty YAML handling**: Define what constitutes "empty or invalid YAML" more precisely
5. **Add circular alias detection**: Prevent aliases from creating circular references
6. **Specify logging fallback**: Define behavior when logging isn't configured by CLI

Once these elements are addressed, the plan will be comprehensive and ready for implementation. The core design is sound and the approach is well-thought-out.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 4-5 hours (slightly higher than estimated due to missing elements)

## Strengths
- Comprehensive YAML schema definition with clear required/optional fields
- Excellent error handling strategy with custom `EvaluatorParseError` exception
- Thorough validation of evaluator names and aliases using regex patterns
- Well-designed conflict resolution (first-wins with logging)
- Detailed test coverage including edge cases and error conditions
- Clear separation of concerns between parsing and discovery
- Good logging strategy using standard Python logging module
- Handles encoding issues explicitly with UTF-8 requirement
- Thoughtful alias handling (None/string/list normalization)

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing import statements in discovery.py implementation (yaml, re modules)
- [CRITICAL] Inconsistent function signature: `discover_local_evaluators()` accepts `Path | None` but implementation shows `base_path: Path | None = None` - this union syntax requires Python 3.10+
- [MEDIUM] No validation that `api_key_env` is a valid environment variable name format
- [MEDIUM] `fallback_model` field is mentioned in schema but not validated in parser
- [MEDIUM] No size limits on YAML files - could cause memory issues with very large files
- [LOW] Logging configuration dependency not clearly stated (relies on CLI setup)
- [LOW] No mention of handling YAML files with BOM (Byte Order Mark)

## Missing or Unclear
- Import statements missing from the discovery.py code blocks
- No specification of Python version compatibility (union types require 3.10+)
- Unclear how `config_file` parameter gets the absolute vs relative path
- No mention of handling symbolic links to YAML files
- Test file location assumes pytest discovery but doesn't specify test runner setup
- No specification of what happens with duplicate aliases across different evaluators

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add explicit import statements to all code blocks in the implementation section
2. Use `Union[Path, None]` or `Optional[Path]` for Python <3.10 compatibility, or specify minimum Python version
3. Add validation for `api_key_env` format (valid environment variable name)
4. Consider adding file size limits (e.g., max 1MB per YAML file)
5. Specify whether `config_file` should store absolute or relative paths
6. Add test case for YAML files with BOM
7. Clarify behavior when the same alias appears in multiple YAML files

## Questions for Plan Author
1. What is the minimum Python version requirement for this project? The `Path | None` syntax requires 3.10+
2. Should `config_file` in EvaluatorConfig store absolute paths or relative to project root?
3. How should the system handle YAML files that are symbolic links to files outside the evaluators directory?
4. Is there a maximum reasonable size limit for YAML files to prevent memory issues?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following changes are needed:

1. **Fix import statements**: Add missing `import yaml` and `import re` to the discovery.py code blocks
2. **Fix type annotations**: Either use `Optional[Path]` or specify Python 3.10+ requirement
3. **Add api_key_env validation**: Validate that api_key_env follows environment variable naming conventions (e.g., uppercase, underscores, no spaces)
4. **Clarify path handling**: Specify whether config_file should be absolute or relative path
5. **Add file size consideration**: Either add a reasonable size limit or document that large files are acceptable

The core design is sound and the implementation approach is well-thought-out. These are primarily technical details that need clarification before implementation begins.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 6-8 hours (higher than estimated due to complexity)

## Strengths
- Clear identification of code duplication problem (~200 lines duplicated)
- Well-structured approach with separation of concerns (runner, config, discovery)
- Comprehensive error handling scenarios covered
- Good abstraction that enables custom evaluators
- Detailed function signatures and return types
- Thorough testing plan with both unit and integration tests
- Clear migration path for existing functionality

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing prompt extraction from shell scripts - the plan references `EVALUATE_PROMPT = """..."""` but doesn't specify how to extract these from existing `.sh` files
- [CRITICAL] Circular import risk - `runner.py` imports from `cli.py` (`load_config`, `validate_evaluation_output`) but `cli.py` will import from `runner.py`
- [CRITICAL] The `builtins.py` file structure shows prompts that need to be extracted but the extraction process isn't defined
- [MEDIUM] Large function `run_evaluator()` (~150+ lines) - could benefit from further decomposition
- [MEDIUM] No validation that custom evaluator YAML configs are compatible with the runner
- [MEDIUM] Platform-specific error handling assumes Windows/Unix but doesn't handle other edge cases
- [LOW] Color constants redefined in runner.py instead of importing from a shared module

## Missing or Unclear
- How exactly will prompts be extracted from existing shell scripts?
- What happens if `validate_evaluation_output()` function doesn't exist or changes signature?
- How will the transition period work - will both old and new implementations coexist?
- Error handling for malformed YAML in custom evaluators
- Specification of what constitutes a "valid" evaluation output
- How will logging/debugging work for the generic runner?

## Specific Recommendations
1. **Extract prompts first**: Create a separate subtask to extract prompts from shell scripts into constants/files before implementing the runner
2. **Break circular imports**: Move shared utilities (`load_config`, `validate_evaluation_output`) to a separate `utils.py` module
3. **Decompose runner function**: Split `run_evaluator()` into smaller functions (~30-50 lines each)
4. **Add validation layer**: Create `validate_evaluator_config()` function to check custom evaluator compatibility
5. **Define output format contract**: Specify exactly what `validate_evaluation_output()` expects
6. **Create shared constants module**: Move color codes and other constants to `adversarial_workflow/constants.py`

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Should the shell script extraction be a prerequisite task, or can it be done inline during this implementation?
2. How do you plan to handle the circular import between `cli.py` and `runner.py`?
3. What's the fallback behavior if a custom evaluator's model/API is unavailable?
4. Should there be a dry-run mode for testing evaluator configs without making API calls?
5. How will this interact with the existing logging infrastructure?

## Approval Conditions
**To approve this plan, the following must be addressed:**

1. **Resolve circular imports**: Specify how `load_config` and `validate_evaluation_output` will be accessed without importing from `cli.py`
2. **Define prompt extraction**: Add specific steps for extracting prompts from existing shell scripts, or make it a prerequisite
3. **Add config validation**: Include validation for custom evaluator configurations
4. **Specify shared utilities**: Define where common utilities will live to avoid code duplication
5. **Break down large functions**: Show how `run_evaluator()` will be decomposed into smaller, testable units

**Additional recommendations for implementation:**
- Consider implementing this in phases: first the infrastructure, then the migration
- Add comprehensive logging for debugging evaluator execution
- Include rollback plan if the generic runner has issues

The core concept is sound and addresses a real need, but the implementation details need refinement to avoid architectural issues.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 6-8 hours (higher than estimated due to complexity)

## Strengths
- Clear architectural vision for eliminating code duplication
- Well-thought-out circular import prevention strategy
- Comprehensive error handling coverage (file validation, API keys, timeouts, rate limits)
- Good separation of concerns between built-in and custom evaluators
- Detailed implementation with specific function signatures
- Thorough testing requirements including both unit and integration tests
- Clear migration path for existing functionality

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] The plan creates a complex hybrid execution model that may be harder to maintain than the current duplication
- [CRITICAL] Missing validation that the extracted utility functions (`load_config`, `validate_evaluation_output`) actually exist in current codebase
- [CRITICAL] The `builtins.py` file requires extracting prompts from shell scripts, but no validation that these prompts exist or are extractable
- [MEDIUM] The `_execute_script` function has a circular import issue - it imports `validate_evaluation_output` from `adversarial_workflow.cli` which contradicts the architectural goal
- [MEDIUM] No error handling for malformed YAML in custom evaluators
- [MEDIUM] The timeout parameter is hardcoded differently in various places (180s default, but scripts may have different expectations)
- [LOW] Large file size thresholds (500/700 lines, 20k tokens) appear arbitrary without justification

## Missing or Unclear
- No specification of what happens if shell scripts don't exist or aren't executable
- Unclear how the `log_prefix` field in `EvaluatorConfig` is populated for built-ins
- Missing details on how existing `.adversarial/config.yml` structure maps to the new `load_config()` function
- No specification of backward compatibility guarantees
- Missing error handling for cases where log directory creation fails
- Unclear what happens if custom evaluator YAML has missing required fields

## Specific Recommendations
1. **Simplify the hybrid approach**: Consider making built-in evaluators use the same YAML-based approach as custom ones, storing their configs in the codebase rather than maintaining shell scripts
2. **Add validation step**: Include a pre-implementation task to verify all referenced functions and files actually exist in the current codebase
3. **Fix circular import**: Move `validate_evaluation_output` to `utils/validation.py` as planned, and update the import in `_execute_script`
4. **Add configuration validation**: Include validation for both project config and evaluator YAML parsing
5. **Standardize timeouts**: Define timeout behavior consistently across built-in and custom evaluators

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Have you verified that `load_config()` and `validate_evaluation_output()` actually exist in the current `cli.py` and can be extracted cleanly?
2. Why maintain the shell script approach for built-ins rather than converting them to the same YAML format as custom evaluators?
3. How will you handle version compatibility if the shell script interface changes?
4. What's the fallback behavior if a built-in evaluator's shell script is missing or corrupted?

## Approval Conditions
**For NEEDS_REVISION approval, address these critical issues:**

1. **Verify current codebase**: Confirm that all referenced functions (`load_config`, `validate_evaluation_output`) exist and can be extracted as planned
2. **Fix circular import**: Correct the import issue in `_execute_script` function
3. **Add missing validation**: Include error handling for malformed YAML, missing shell scripts, and failed directory creation
4. **Clarify built-in evaluator data**: Either verify that prompts can be extracted from shell scripts OR pivot to a simpler approach where built-ins also use YAML configs
5. **Define backward compatibility**: Specify what guarantees are made about existing functionality during and after migration

The core architectural approach is sound, but the implementation details need refinement to ensure reliability and maintainability.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 6-8 hours (higher than estimated due to complexity)

## Strengths
- Excellent architectural decision to prevent circular imports by moving utilities to `utils/`
- Clear separation between built-in and custom evaluator execution paths
- Comprehensive error handling for common failure modes (missing files, API keys, rate limits)
- Well-structured code with proper separation of concerns
- Detailed acceptance criteria and testing requirements
- Good migration path preserving existing functionality

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] The `builtins.py` approach requires extracting prompts from shell scripts, but the plan doesn't specify how to do this or validate the extraction is correct
- [CRITICAL] Built-in evaluators still use shell scripts but custom evaluators bypass them - this creates two completely different execution paths that are hard to maintain
- [CRITICAL] The plan creates `utils/validation.py` but references `validate_evaluation_output()` - unclear if this function exists or needs to be created
- [MEDIUM] File size checking logic (`_check_file_size`) uses simplistic token estimation (content length / 4) which may be inaccurate
- [MEDIUM] No specification for how to handle different file encodings or binary files
- [MEDIUM] The timeout handling doesn't distinguish between different types of timeouts (network vs processing)
- [LOW] Color constants duplication across modules could be avoided with a single import

## Missing or Unclear
- How exactly will prompts be extracted from existing shell scripts? Are they embedded as comments, heredocs, or separate files?
- What happens if `validate_evaluation_output()` doesn't exist yet? Is this function being moved or created?
- How will the transition work if built-in evaluators need to be updated? Will both shell scripts and YAML configs need maintenance?
- No specification for handling non-UTF-8 files or files with special characters
- Missing details on how temporary files are cleaned up in error scenarios
- No mention of logging strategy for debugging failed evaluations

## Specific Recommendations
1. **Simplify the dual execution path**: Consider making built-in evaluators use the same YAML-based approach as custom ones, eliminating shell script dependency entirely
2. **Specify prompt extraction process**: Detail exactly how prompts will be extracted from shell scripts and how to verify they're complete
3. **Add file encoding handling**: Specify how to detect and handle different file encodings gracefully
4. **Improve token estimation**: Use a proper tokenizer library or at least a more sophisticated estimation method
5. **Add cleanup specifications**: Detail how temporary files and partial outputs are cleaned up on failures
6. **Consider backwards compatibility**: Plan for gradual migration rather than immediate replacement of shell scripts

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Why maintain two different execution paths (shell scripts vs direct aider calls) instead of standardizing on one approach?
2. Have you verified that all necessary prompts can be cleanly extracted from the existing shell scripts?
3. How will you handle the case where a built-in evaluator's shell script has logic beyond just calling aider (preprocessing, postprocessing, etc.)?
4. Should the `validate_evaluation_output()` function be created as part of this task or does it already exist?
5. What's the long-term vision - will shell scripts eventually be deprecated entirely?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following changes are needed:

1. **Clarify prompt extraction**: Add a detailed section explaining how prompts will be extracted from shell scripts, including examples and validation steps
2. **Specify validation function**: Clarify whether `validate_evaluation_output()` exists or needs to be created, and if created, provide its specification
3. **Add file handling details**: Specify how different file encodings and edge cases (empty files, binary files, etc.) will be handled
4. **Improve error recovery**: Add specifications for cleanup of temporary files and partial outputs in error scenarios
5. **Consider execution path unification**: Either justify why two execution paths are necessary or propose a plan to unify them
6. **Add integration testing strategy**: Specify how to test the interaction between built-in and custom evaluators without requiring API keys for CI

The core architecture is sound, but these implementation details need clarification before development begins to avoid mid-implementation surprises and rework.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 4-5 hours (higher than estimated due to missing elements)

## Strengths
- Clear architectural approach using dynamic subparser registration
- Good separation of concerns between discovery and execution
- Comprehensive test plan covering integration, backwards compatibility, and edge cases
- Thoughtful performance considerations with caching options
- Well-defined acceptance criteria
- Preserves backwards compatibility for existing CLI and Python API
- Handles alias registration elegantly with duplicate prevention

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing error handling for malformed evaluator configs during CLI startup
- [CRITICAL] No specification for handling evaluator discovery failures (missing dependencies, invalid YAML, etc.)
- [CRITICAL] Command dispatch logic has potential conflicts - what if a custom evaluator name matches a static command?
- [MEDIUM] Performance impact not quantified - "fast (<100ms)" is vague without baseline
- [MEDIUM] No rollback strategy if dynamic registration fails partially
- [MEDIUM] Missing validation that required evaluator fields exist before registration
- [LOW] Help text formatting could be improved with better grouping of evaluator vs system commands

## Missing or Unclear
- Error handling strategy when `get_all_evaluators()` fails during CLI startup
- Behavior when evaluator config is invalid (missing required fields, bad YAML syntax)
- Priority/ordering of commands in help output (should evaluators be grouped separately?)
- Integration with existing argument parsing for global flags (--version, etc.)
- Specification of what happens if evaluator discovery is slow (>100ms) - should it timeout?
- Details on how `run_evaluator()` function signature and error handling works
- Migration path for any existing hardcoded evaluator logic that needs removal

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add explicit error handling section covering evaluator discovery failures, malformed configs, and graceful degradation
2. Specify command name collision resolution (e.g., static commands take precedence over evaluators)
3. Add validation step before registering evaluators to ensure required fields are present
4. Consider grouping evaluators separately in help output for better UX
5. Add timeout mechanism for evaluator discovery to prevent CLI startup hangs
6. Specify the exact interface contract for `run_evaluator()` function
7. Add integration test for CLI startup performance with many evaluators

## Questions for Plan Author
1. How should the CLI behave if evaluator discovery fails completely - should it still start with just static commands?
2. What's the expected behavior if a custom evaluator has the same name as a built-in command like "init" or "check"?
3. Should there be a maximum number of evaluators that can be registered to prevent help output from becoming unwieldy?
4. How will global CLI flags (--version, --help) interact with the dynamic subparser registration?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following must be addressed:

1. **Add Error Handling Section**: Specify behavior for evaluator discovery failures, malformed configs, and partial failures
2. **Define Command Collision Resolution**: Explicit rules for when evaluator names conflict with static commands
3. **Add Validation Requirements**: Specify what validation occurs before registering an evaluator as a CLI command
4. **Clarify run_evaluator Interface**: Document the expected function signature, return values, and error handling
5. **Add Performance Constraints**: Define specific timeout values and fallback behavior for slow discovery
6. **Expand Test Coverage**: Add tests for error conditions, command collisions, and performance edge cases

The core architectural approach is sound, but these implementation details are critical for a robust solution.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 4-5 hours (higher than estimated due to missing pieces)

## Strengths
- Comprehensive error handling strategy with graceful degradation
- Clear priority order for command name collision resolution
- Well-thought-out backwards compatibility preservation
- Detailed code examples showing the implementation approach
- Good test coverage plan with specific test cases
- Performance considerations addressed upfront
- Clear acceptance criteria and migration notes

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing import structure - plan doesn't specify where `get_all_evaluators` and `run_evaluator` are imported from
- [CRITICAL] Circular import risk - CLI importing from evaluators module that may depend on CLI utilities
- [CRITICAL] No specification of how `run_evaluator` function should work or what it returns
- [MEDIUM] Command dispatch logic is complex and could be simplified with a registry pattern
- [MEDIUM] Error handling for evaluator execution failures not specified
- [MEDIUM] No mention of how to handle evaluators that require different argument patterns
- [LOW] Performance target of <100ms for discovery may be optimistic depending on file I/O

## Missing or Unclear
- How `run_evaluator(config, file, timeout)` is implemented - this is a key dependency
- What happens if an evaluator crashes during execution vs. discovery
- How timeout handling works in practice (process killing, graceful shutdown, etc.)
- Whether evaluators can have custom CLI arguments beyond file and timeout
- Integration with existing logging/output formatting systems
- How this interacts with the agent subcommand structure mentioned briefly

## Specific Recommendations
1. **Define the evaluator execution interface first** - Specify exactly how `run_evaluator` works, what it returns, and how errors are handled
2. **Use a command registry pattern** - Instead of complex if/elif chains, register commands in a dictionary for cleaner dispatch
3. **Add evaluator argument validation** - Ensure evaluator configs specify their expected CLI arguments
4. **Specify import locations** - Make clear which modules contain `get_all_evaluators` and `run_evaluator`
5. **Add integration test for full workflow** - Test discovery → registration → execution end-to-end

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Should evaluators be able to define custom CLI arguments beyond file and timeout?
2. How should evaluator execution errors be formatted and displayed to users?
3. Is there a reason to keep the existing evaluate/proofread/review functions as wrappers vs. removing them entirely?
4. Should there be a way to disable/enable specific evaluators without deleting their config files?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following must be addressed:

1. **Specify the evaluator execution interface** - Document the signature, return values, and error handling for `run_evaluator`
2. **Clarify import structure** - Show exactly where `get_all_evaluators` and `run_evaluator` come from and ensure no circular imports
3. **Add error handling for execution phase** - Not just discovery, but what happens when an evaluator fails to run
4. **Simplify command dispatch** - Consider a registry pattern instead of complex conditional logic
5. **Add end-to-end integration test** - Verify the complete flow works together

The core approach is sound, but these implementation details need clarification before coding begins.

## Strengths
- Clear problem identification with concrete before/after examples
- Root cause analysis is accurate and well-explained
- Solution approach using `dotenv_values()` is sound and elegant
- Good documentation of the dependency on ADV-0021
- Includes both implementation steps and testing approach
- Acceptance criteria are measurable and specific

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Import placement could cause issues - importing `dotenv_values` inside the conditional block is unusual and may impact performance/readability
- [CRITICAL] No verification that `dotenv_values()` handles malformed .env files the same way as `load_dotenv()`
- [MEDIUM] Test assumes specific .env format but doesn't verify edge cases (empty file, comments, malformed entries)
- [MEDIUM] No consideration of what happens if .env file exists but is unreadable (permissions)
- [LOW] Message text changes from "loaded" to just "found" - this is a user-facing change that should be explicitly acknowledged

## Missing or Unclear
- Error handling strategy for `dotenv_values()` failures
- Behavior specification for edge cases (empty .env, malformed entries, permission errors)
- Whether the message change from "loaded" to "found" is intentional and acceptable
- No mention of whether existing error handling around .env loading needs updates
- Import strategy - should `dotenv_values` be imported at module level or locally?

## Specific Recommendations
1. Move `from dotenv import dotenv_values` to the top of the file with other imports for consistency
2. Add error handling around `dotenv_values()` call to match robustness of current implementation
3. Add test cases for edge scenarios: empty .env file, malformed .env file, permission denied
4. Explicitly document the user-facing message change from "loaded" to "found" and get approval
5. Consider wrapping `dotenv_values()` in try/except to gracefully handle file read errors

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Is the message change from "found and loaded" to "found" intentional? Should users be informed that variables are already loaded?
2. Should we maintain the same error handling behavior as the current `load_dotenv()` approach?
3. Have you verified that `dotenv_values()` handles all the same .env file formats and edge cases as `load_dotenv()`?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, please address:
1. **Add error handling specification** - How should `dotenv_values()` failures be handled?
2. **Clarify import placement** - Move import to module level or justify local import
3. **Add edge case testing** - Include tests for empty files, malformed files, permission errors
4. **Document message change** - Explicitly acknowledge the user-facing text change and confirm it's acceptable
5. **Verify behavioral equivalence** - Confirm `dotenv_values()` handles all cases that `load_dotenv()` currently handles

The core approach is solid, but these implementation details need clarification to ensure a robust solution.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 4-5 hours (higher than estimated due to missing elements)

## Strengths
- Clear problem statement with concrete data showing timeout issues
- Well-structured implementation plan with logical phases
- Good precedence hierarchy: CLI > YAML > default
- Comprehensive test cases covering various scenarios
- Detailed acceptance criteria with measurable outcomes
- Thoughtful maximum timeout limit (600s) to prevent runaway processes
- Good documentation of file locations and line numbers

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] No validation that the timeout field placement in EvaluatorConfig won't break existing serialization/deserialization
- [CRITICAL] Missing error handling for the case where CLI timeout exceeds 600s (only YAML validation is specified)
- [CRITICAL] No consideration of backward compatibility - what happens to existing evaluator configs without timeout field?
- [MEDIUM] The plan assumes specific line numbers which may be outdated by implementation time
- [MEDIUM] No discussion of how this interacts with existing timeout mechanisms in the runner
- [MEDIUM] Missing integration test that actually runs an evaluator with the new timeout
- [LOW] No consideration of logging the actual timeout being used for debugging

## Missing or Unclear
- How does this interact with any existing timeout handling in `runner.py`?
- What happens if the evaluator process is killed mid-execution due to timeout?
- Should there be different timeout defaults for different model types?
- How will users discover what timeout value they should use?
- Is there any cleanup needed when a timeout occurs?
- Should the timeout be validated against model-specific recommendations?

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add CLI timeout validation (>600s should error or clamp with warning, consistent with YAML behavior)
2. Include integration test that actually runs an evaluator with custom timeout, not just unit tests
3. Add logging of the actual timeout value being used at evaluation start
4. Consider adding a `--list-timeouts` or similar command to show timeout values for all evaluators
5. Specify what happens to in-flight API requests when timeout occurs
6. Add migration consideration: ensure existing configs without timeout field continue to work

## Questions for Plan Author
1. How does this timeout interact with any HTTP client timeouts or API-level timeouts?
2. Should there be model-specific timeout recommendations documented somewhere?
3. What's the user experience when a timeout occurs - do they get helpful error messages?
4. Are there any existing timeout mechanisms in the runner that need to be coordinated with this change?
5. Should the timeout be configurable at the workflow level (affecting all evaluators) as well?

## Approval Conditions
To approve this plan, the following must be addressed:

1. **Add CLI timeout validation**: Specify how CLI timeout values >600s are handled (error vs clamp)
2. **Add integration test**: Include at least one test that actually runs an evaluator with custom timeout
3. **Clarify interaction with existing timeout handling**: Document how this relates to any existing timeout mechanisms
4. **Add logging**: Specify that the actual timeout value should be logged when evaluation starts
5. **Address backward compatibility**: Confirm that existing configs without timeout field will work unchanged
6. **Specify timeout error handling**: What happens when timeout occurs (cleanup, error messages, etc.)

The core approach is sound, but these gaps need to be filled to ensure robust implementation.

- Good backward compatibility considerations
- Comprehensive test strategy covering unit, integration, and CLI scenarios
- Clear acceptance criteria and success metrics
- Thoughtful precedence hierarchy (CLI > YAML > default)
- Good error handling for validation cases

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] Missing validation for the existing codebase structure - plan assumes file locations and function signatures without verification
- [CRITICAL] No consideration of concurrent evaluations or thread safety implications
- [MEDIUM] Timeout clamping behavior inconsistency between YAML and CLI (YAML clamps silently after warning, CLI behavior unclear)
- [MEDIUM] No rollback strategy if implementation breaks existing evaluators
- [MEDIUM] Integration test design is vague - "mock/lightweight evaluator" needs concrete specification
- [LOW] Documentation file path is uncertain ("docs/evaluators.md or equivalent")

## Missing or Unclear
- How will the timeout validation interact with existing CLI argument parsing?
- What happens if an evaluator YAML has both old and new timeout specifications?
- Error message consistency across YAML parsing vs CLI validation
- Impact on any existing timeout-related logging or monitoring
- Behavior when timeout=0 is specified (should this disable timeout entirely?)
- Whether the 600s maximum is a hard requirement or configurable

## Specific Recommendations
1. Add a Phase 0 to verify current codebase structure and document any deviations from assumptions
2. Specify exact error message formats for consistency across YAML and CLI validation
3. Define the mock evaluator specification for integration tests (e.g., a simple script that sleeps for a configurable duration)
4. Add explicit handling for timeout=0 case (disable timeout vs validation error)
5. Consider adding a configuration validation command to help users test their YAML files
6. Add logging of which timeout source is being used (CLI override, YAML config, or default)

## Questions for Plan Author
1. Should timeout=0 disable the timeout entirely, or should it be treated as invalid?
2. Is the 600s maximum a business requirement, or could it be made configurable via environment variable?
3. How should the system behave if multiple evaluators are running concurrently with different timeouts?
4. Should there be any timeout recommendations or warnings for specific models in the documentation?

1. **Add Phase 0: Codebase Verification**

   - Document any structural differences from the plan assumptions
   - Confirm the dataclass field insertion location in EvaluatorConfig

2. **Clarify timeout=0 behavior**
   - Explicitly state whether timeout=0 disables timeout or is invalid
   - Add this case to validation logic and test cases

3. **Specify integration test details**
   - Define the exact mock evaluator implementation (suggest a simple Python script that accepts a sleep duration)
   - Specify how the test will verify timeout values flow through the stack

4. **Standardize error messages**
   - Provide exact error message templates for all validation failures
   - Ensure consistency between YAML parsing and CLI validation messages

5. **Add timeout source logging**
   - Specify that the system should log which timeout source is being used
   - Add this to the acceptance criteria

6. **Address edge cases**
   - What happens if YAML contains `timeout: null` or `timeout: ""` 
   - How to handle YAML parsing errors specifically for the timeout field

Once these items are addressed, the plan will be ready for implementation. The core approach is sound and the phased implementation strategy is well thought out.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** HIGH
**Estimated Implementation Time:** 3-4 days

## Strengths
- The plan provides a comprehensive overview of the CLI commands and their intended functionality.
- It includes detailed usage examples and expected behaviors for each command.
- The architecture context and file structure are well-defined, providing a clear guide for implementation.

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] The plan lacks detailed error handling strategies for network failures beyond caching, such as handling partial downloads or corrupted files.
- [MEDIUM] The plan does not specify how to handle schema validation failures when installing or updating evaluators.
- [LOW] The caching mechanism's TTL and invalidation strategy could be more flexible to accommodate different use cases.

## Missing or Unclear
- The plan does not address how to handle edge cases, such as what happens if the index.json format changes or if the evaluator library repository structure changes.
- There is no mention of how to handle potential conflicts with existing evaluator configurations beyond the `--force` flag.
- The plan does not specify how the CLI will be tested in environments with limited or no internet access.

## Specific Recommendations
1. Include a detailed error handling strategy for network-related issues, including retries and handling of partial downloads.
2. Define a clear process for schema validation failures, including user feedback and potential rollback mechanisms.
3. Consider implementing a more flexible caching strategy, possibly allowing users to configure the TTL.

## Questions for Plan Author
1. How will the CLI handle changes in the index.json format or evaluator library structure?
2. What is the plan for testing the CLI in environments with limited or no internet access?
3. Are there any plans to support additional configuration options for caching, such as user-defined TTLs?

## Approval Conditions
- Address the critical and medium concerns, particularly around error handling and schema validation.
- Provide clarity on handling changes in the library's structure and format.
- Consider the recommendations for a more flexible caching strategy.

## Evaluation Summary
**Verdict:** NEEDS_REVISION
**Confidence:** MEDIUM

## Strengths
- The plan provides a comprehensive overview of the CLI commands and their intended functionality.
- It includes detailed usage examples and expected behaviors for each command.
- The plan outlines a robust error handling strategy, including network errors and schema validation failures.

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] The plan lacks specific details on how the CLI commands will be integrated into the existing codebase, particularly in terms of file and function names.
- [MEDIUM] The caching mechanism's implementation details are not fully fleshed out, especially regarding cache invalidation and user-configurable TTL.
- [LOW] The plan does not address potential performance issues with large `index.json` files.

## Missing or Unclear
- The plan does not specify the exact sequence of changes needed to implement the new features.
- There is no mention of how the new functionality will be documented for end-users.
- The plan assumes the existence of certain dependencies and structures without verifying their presence or compatibility.

## Specific Recommendations
1. Provide a more detailed implementation plan, including specific file and function names, to ensure clarity and ease of integration.
2. Consider alternative caching strategies that might offer better performance or flexibility.
3. Add steps for documenting the new CLI features for end-users, including updates to any existing documentation.

## Questions for Plan Author
1. How will the new CLI commands be integrated into the existing codebase? Are there specific files or modules that will be affected?
2. What is the plan for handling large `index.json` files in terms of performance and memory usage?
3. Are there any trade-offs considered between using a local cache versus always fetching the latest data from the library?

## Approval Conditions
- The plan needs to include a detailed implementation sequence with specific file and function names.
- Clarify the caching mechanism, including cache invalidation and user-configurable TTL.
- Address the documentation needs for the new CLI features.
