####   
#### # ADV-0052: Restructure scripts/ to core/ + local/  
####   
#### **Status**: Todo  
#### **Priority**: High  
#### **Type**: Infrastructure  
#### **Estimated Effort**: 60 minutes  
#### **Created**: 2026-03-08  
#### **Updated**: 2026-03-09  
#### **Depends On**: ~~ASK-0042~~ — completed in agentive-starter-kit v0.4.0  
#### **Parent**: KIT-0024 (Core Scripts Standardization)  
####   
#### ## Summary  
####   
#### Adopt the `scripts/core/` + `scripts/local/` + `scripts/optional/` layout  
#### from agentive-starter-kit v0.4.0 in adversarial-workflow. Copy 14 core  
#### scripts, update all references, and unbreak 6 broken slash commands.  
####   
#### **Upstream source**: `agentive-starter-kit` tag `v0.4.0` (core scripts v1.2.0)  
#### **Migration guide**: `docs/UPGRADE-0.4.0.md` in agentive-starter-kit  
####   
#### ## Current State  
####   
#### - 6 scripts in flat `scripts/` directory (should be 14)  
#### - **6/7 slash commands are broken** — reference scripts that don't exist  
#### - `ci-check.sh`, `verify-setup.sh`, `project`, `validate_task_status.py` are outdated  
#### - Full analysis: `.agent-context/research/SCRIPTS-SYNC-ANALYSIS.md`  
####   
#### ## Scope  
####   
#### ### 1. Create directory structure  
####   
#### ```  
#### scripts/  
####   ├── core/                        ◀── 14 files from agentive-starter-kit v0.4.0  
####   │   ├── VERSION                  (contains "1.2.0")  
####   │   ├── __init__.py  
####   │   ├── project  
####   │   ├── ci-check.sh  
####   │   ├── verify-ci.sh  
####   │   ├── verify-setup.sh  
####   │   ├── check-bots.sh  
####   │   ├── wait-for-bots.sh  
####   │   ├── gh-review-helper.sh  
####   │   ├── preflight-check.sh  
####   │   ├── check-sync.sh           ◀── NEW: verifies core scripts match upstream  
####   │   ├── pattern_lint.py  
####   │   ├── validate_task_status.py  
####   │   └── logging_config.py  
####   ├── local/                       ◀── ADW-specific (currently empty)  
####   │   └── .gitkeep  
####   ├── optional/                    ◀── Opt-in scripts (copy from ASK if needed)  
####   │   └── .gitkeep  
####   ├── .core-manifest.json  
####   └── README.md  
#### ```  
####   
#### ### 2. Copy core scripts from ASK v0.4.0  
####   
#### Clone or fetch agentive-starter-kit at tag v0.4.0 and copy all 14 files  
#### from `scripts/core/` into `scripts/core/`.  
####   
#### Copy `.core-manifest.json` from ASK `scripts/.core-manifest.json`.  
####   
#### **No interim approach needed** — ASK-0042 is complete.  
####   
#### ### 3. Fix `project` script path resolution  
####   
#### The `project` script resolves repo root via `Path(__file__).resolve()`.  
#### After moving from `scripts/project` to `scripts/core/project`, it needs  
#### one extra `.parent`:  
####   
#### ```python  
#### # Before (scripts/project):  
#### project_dir = Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent  
####   
#### # After (scripts/core/project):  
#### project_dir = Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent.parent  
#### ```  
####   
#### Two occurrences: `cmd_setup()` and `main()`. Both must be updated.  
####   
#### ### 4. Remove old scripts from root  
####   
#### Delete from `scripts/` root: `ci-check.sh`, `logging_config.py`,  
#### `validate_task_status.py`, `verify-setup.sh`, `project`, `__init__.py`,  
#### `__pycache__/`.  
####   
#### ### 5. Update all references  
####   
#### Files that need `./scripts/<name>` → `./scripts/core/<name>`:  
####   
#### | Location | Files | Count |  
#### |----------|-------|-------|  
#### | `.claude/commands/*.md` | check-ci, check-bots, wait-for-bots, triage-threads, preflight, commit-push-pr, start-task | 7 |  
#### | `.claude/agents/*.md` | feature-developer, feature-developer-v3, code-reviewer, test-runner, security-reviewer, agent-creator, document-reviewer, planner, planner2, AGENT-TEMPLATE, TASK-STARTER-TEMPLATE | 11 |  
#### | `.pre-commit-config.yaml` | pattern_lint.py path (if referenced) | 1 |  
#### | `.agent-context/workflows/*.md` | script references | ~3 |  
#### | `CLAUDE.md` | script paths in tables | 1 |  
#### | `tests/` | import paths, `_script_path` definitions, mock `.parent` chains | ~2 |  
####   
#### **Verification grep** (run after all updates):  
#### ```bash  
#### grep -rn 'scripts/project\b\|scripts/ci-check\|scripts/verify-\|scripts/pattern_lint\|scripts/check-bots\|scripts/wait-for\|scripts/gh-review\|scripts/preflight' \

#### ```

- **Issue**: Summary says "unbreak 6 broken slash commands" but Scope section 5 lists 7 files in `.claude/commands/*.md`
- **Remediation**: Clarify whether it's 6 or 7 slash commands that need fixing

- **Location**: Directory structure comment
- **Issue**: Says "14 files from agentive-starter-kit v0.4.0" but the tree shows 13 items (VERSION + 12 scripts). The comment "(13 scripts + VERSION)" in Acceptance Criteria clarifies this, but the initial statement is ambiguous.
- **Remediation**: Change "14 files" to "13 scripts + VERSION file (14 total)" for clarity

- **Location**: Known Pitfalls section, item 5
- **Issue**: Mentions `start-daemons.sh` and `test-critical.sh` need handling but doesn't specify which agent files reference them
- **Remediation**: Add a note to grep for these during Step 5 updates, or list affected files

### [LOW]: Missing estimated time for reference updates
- **Location**: Scope section 5
- **Issue**: Step 5 (Update all references) is complex with ~25 files to update, but overall task is estimated at 60 minutes
- **Remediation**: Consider breaking out reference updates as a separate task or increasing estimate

#### # ADV-0052: Restructure scripts/ to core/ + local/  
####   
#### **Status**: Todo  
#### **Priority**: High  
#### **Type**: Infrastructure  
#### **Estimated Effort**: 60 minutes  
#### **Created**: 2026-03-08  
#### **Updated**: 2026-03-09  
#### **Depends On**: ~~ASK-0042~~ — completed in agentive-starter-kit v0.4.0  
#### **Parent**: KIT-0024 (Core Scripts Standardization)  
####   
#### ## Summary  
####   
#### Adopt the `scripts/core/` + `scripts/local/` + `scripts/optional/` layout  
#### from agentive-starter-kit v0.4.0 in adversarial-workflow. Copy 14 core  
#### scripts, update all references, and unbreak 6 broken slash commands.  
####   
#### **Upstream source**: `agentive-starter-kit` tag `v0.4.0` (core scripts v1.2.0)  
#### **Migration guide**: `docs/UPGRADE-0.4.0.md` in agentive-starter-kit  
####   
#### ## Current State  
####   
#### - 6 scripts in flat `scripts/` directory (should be 14)  
#### - **6/7 slash commands are broken** — reference scripts that don't exist  
#### - `ci-check.sh`, `verify-setup.sh`, `project`, `validate_task_status.py` are outdated  
#### - Full analysis: `.agent-context/research/SCRIPTS-SYNC-ANALYSIS.md`  
####   
#### ## Scope  
####   
#### ### 1. Create directory structure  
####   
#### ```  
#### scripts/  
####   ├── core/                        ◀── 14 files from agentive-starter-kit v0.4.0  
####   │   ├── VERSION                  (contains "1.2.0")  
####   │   ├── __init__.py  
####   │   ├── project  
####   │   ├── ci-check.sh  
####   │   ├── verify-ci.sh

####   │   ├── wait-for-bots.sh  
####   │   ├── gh-review-helper.sh  
####   │   ├── preflight-check.sh  
####   │   ├── check-sync.sh           ◀── NEW: verifies core scripts match upstream  
####   │   ├── pattern_lint.py  
####   │   ├── validate_task_status.py  
####   │   └── logging_config.py  
####   ├── local/                       ◀── ADW-specific (currently empty)  
####   │   └── .gitkeep  
####   ├── optional/                    ◀── Opt-in scripts (copy from ASK if needed)  
####   │   └── .gitkeep  
####   ├── .core-manifest.json  
####   └── README.md  
#### ```

#### from `scripts/core/` into `scripts/core/`.  
####   
#### Copy `.core-manifest.json` from ASK `scripts/.core-manifest.json`.  
####   
#### **No interim approach needed** — ASK-0042 is complete.  
####   
#### ### 3. Fix `project` script path resolution  
####   
#### The `project` script resolves repo root via `Path(__file__).resolve()`.  
#### After moving from `scripts/project` to `scripts/core/project`, it needs  
#### one extra `.parent`:  
####   
#### ```python  
#### # Before (scripts/project):  
#### project_dir = Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent  
####   
#### # After (scripts/core/project):  
#### project_dir = Path(__file__).resolve().parent.parent.parent  
#### ```  
####   
#### Two occurrences: `cmd_setup()` and `main()`. Both must be updated.

#### `__pycache__/`.

### Quick Assessment

| Dimension | Rating | Note |
|-----------|--------|------|
| Clarity | Clear | The goal, steps, and acceptance criteria are exceptionally clear. |
| Architectural fit | Good | Aligns with `agentive-starter-kit` standards, improving script organization and maintainability. |
| Dependencies | Resolved | Explicitly states `ASK-0042` is complete, no other external dependencies are immediately apparent. |
| Risk level | Medium | High impact refactoring across many files, but risks are well-identified and mitigation strategies are proposed. |
| Test strategy | Strong | Comprehensive verification steps and acceptance criteria covering functionality, linting, and internal consistency. |
| Scope | Right-sized | The scope is appropriate for a single, well-defined infrastructure task, bundling related changes. |

### Findings

**[LOW]: Verification Grep Redundancy**
- **What**: The "Verification grep" command explicitly includes `--include='*.toml'` but no TOML files are listed in the "Files that need update" table for `scripts/` references. While not harmful, it might be unnecessary.
- **Why it matters**: Minor inefficiency in the verification step, but otherwise harmless.
- **Suggestion**: Review if `toml` files truly need to be included in the verification grep. If no script references are expected there, it can be removed.

**[LOW]: Clarification on "NEW: verifies core scripts match upstream"**
- **What**: Step 1 lists `check-sync.sh` as "NEW: verifies core scripts match upstream". It would be good to confirm how this script determines "upstream" and what actions it might take or suggest.
- **Why it matters**: Understanding the exact function and assumptions of `check-sync.sh` is important for maintaining consistency and potentially automating updates in the future.
- **Suggestion**: Briefly elaborate on how `check-sync.sh` operates, e.g., does it compare against a local clone of ASK, a remote URL, or a cached manifest?

### Questions for the Author
1. For step 2 ("Copy core scripts from ASK v0.4.0"), what is the preferred method for "Clone or fetch agentive-starter-kit at tag v0.4.0"? Should the implementer clone it specifically for this task, or is there an existing local clone that should be used?
2. The "Known Pitfalls" mentions "DK002 lint rule — new rule flags `open()` without `encoding=`. May need `encoding="utf-8"` additions". Is this something that should be addressed as part of this task, or is it a separate linting task to be handled later? If it's part of this task, it should be added to the Acceptance Criteria.
3. Regarding "Agent files reference non-core scripts — `start-daemons.sh`, `test-critical.sh` are not core scripts. These either go in `local/` or references are removed". What is the definitive decision for these specific scripts (`start-daemons.sh`, `test-critical.sh`)? Should they be moved to `scripts/local/` or have their references removed?

### Verdict

- **NEEDS_REVISION**: The plan is exceptionally well-detailed and robust. The findings are minor and the questions are primarily for clarification and confirm scope boundaries. Addressing these will make the plan even more bulletproof before implementation.

| Test strategy | Strong | Comprehensive verification steps and acceptance criteria, including a specific `grep` command and passing CI/pre-commit. |
| Scope | Right-sized | The task is a single, cohesive architectural refactoring. |

### Findings

**[MEDIUM]: Estimated Effort Understated**
- **What**: The estimated effort of 60 minutes appears optimistic given the scope of changes, which includes creating directories, copying 14 files, updating a Python script in two places, deleting multiple existing scripts, updating references across at least 25 different files/templates (MD, YML, PY), updating test mocks, and performing extensive verification (7 distinct checks, including `pytest` and `pre-commit`).
- **Why it matters**: Underestimating the effort can lead to rushed implementation, incomplete reference updates, and insufficient verification, potentially introducing new bugs or leaving the system in an unstable state. This could increase the total time and effort spent on bug fixing and re-work.
- **Suggestion**: Re-evaluate the estimated effort, considering allocating 2-4 hours to allow for careful execution, thorough reference updates, and comprehensive verification/debugging.

**[LOW]: Clarity on `scripts/__init__.py` Deletion**
- **What**: Step 4 includes `__init__.py` in the list of files to be deleted from the `scripts/` root. While `__pycache__/` removal is standard cleanup, the removal of `__init__.py` implies that the `scripts/` root itself is no longer intended to be a Python package. This is likely the case given `scripts/core/__init__.py` is being introduced.
- **Why it matters**: If any existing Python code (outside the listed files for reference updates) relies on `scripts/` being a Python package (e.g., `import scripts.some_module`), its removal could cause import errors.
- **Suggestion**: Confirm that the `scripts/__init__.py` file at the root is indeed obsolete and its removal will not inadvertently break any Python imports that might expect `scripts/` to be a Python package. (This is a minor clarification, as the plan's overall context suggests this is intended.)

### Questions for the Author
- The "Known Pitfalls" section explicitly mentions removing references to `start-daemons.sh` and `test-critical.sh` from agent files. Are there any other existing non-core scripts that are referenced elsewhere in the codebase which should *not* be migrated to `scripts/core/` and whose references also need to be removed or updated accordingly? The provided `grep` pattern is good, but confirming this can prevent omissions.

| Dimension | Rating | Note |
|:------------------|:-----------|:----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|
| Clarity | Clear | Goal, steps, and acceptance criteria are very well-defined. |
| Architectural fit | Good | Explicitly aligns with an established upstream architecture. |
| Dependencies | Resolved | Upstream dependency (`ASK-0042`) is completed, and instructions for obtaining source scripts are clear. |
| Risk level | Medium | Inherent complexity of a large-scale refactoring; well-mitigated by planning but some minor areas could introduce friction. |
| Test strategy | Strong | Comprehensive verification steps, including a targeted `grep` and checks against core functionality. |
| Scope | Right-sized | Estimated effort aligns with the detailed scope outlined. |

### Findings

**[MEDIUM]: Python Module Resolution after `scripts/__init__.py` Removal**
- **What**: Step 4 details removing `scripts/__init__.py` and mentions verifying "no existing imports use `import scripts.xxx`". This critical verification is currently a note rather than an explicit, trackable step or acceptance criterion.
- **Why it matters**: If `scripts/__init__.py` is removed while Python code (e.g., in `src/` or `tests/`) still attempts `import scripts.some_module`, it will lead to `ModuleNotFoundError` and block successful verification, potentially causing confusion or requiring unplanned fixes.
- **Suggestion**:
    1.  Elevate the check for `import scripts.xxx` statements into a distinct sub-step within "4. Remove old scripts from root", to be performed *before* deleting `scripts/__init__.py`.
    2.  Add an explicit acceptance criterion to confirm that no such imports exist after the migration.

**[LOW]: Immediate `pre-commit` Failure Due to `DK002` Lint Rule**
- **What**: Pitfall 4 notes that the `DK002` lint rule (for `open()` without `encoding=`) is out of scope. However, copying `pattern_lint.py` (which presumably includes this rule) and then running `pre-commit run --all-files` during verification might immediately flag existing violations in the codebase.
- **Why it matters**: A failing `pre-commit` check can halt the verification process and introduce friction, requiring a decision outside the current task's scope (e.g., disable the rule, or fix violations).
- **Suggestion**: Explicitly add a guidance note within the "7. Verify" section on how to handle potential `DK002` lint failures. For example: "If `pre-commit run --all-files` fails due to `DK002` violations, acknowledge them but do not consider them blocking for *this task's* verification, as they are out of scope. A follow-up task will address them." (Alternatively, consider a temporary disablement of the rule for this task's `pre-commit` configuration).

### Questions for the Author
1.  Regarding Pitfall 5 ("Non-core script references" like `start-daemons.sh` and `test-critical.sh`): The plan states these references should be "removed." Is it the implementer's responsibility to proactively search for and remove these references from the relevant files (e.g., `.agent-context/agents/*.md`) during Step 5, or are they expected to be caught by the generic `grep` and then manually identified and removed?
2.  For file operations in Steps 2 (Copy core scripts) and 4 (Remove old scripts): Will `git add` and `git rm` be used directly to track these changes, or is a simpler file system `cp`/`rm` followed by a blanket `git add -A` and then `git rm` for the deleted files implied? Clarifying the expected Git operations ensures a clean history.

### Verdict

- **NEEDS_REVISION**

#### You are an adversarial code reviewer. Your job is to find bugs — edge cases, boundary  
#### conditions, and logic errors. Think like a fuzzer: "How could this break?"

#### Do NOT verify acceptance criteria or check style. Focus only on correctness.

#### ## Review Focus

#### For each function or method in the changed code (if the change is non-code such as config, YAML, or markdown, focus on structural correctness, invalid values, and broken references instead):

####    boundary values. List at least 3 per function.  
#### 2. **Trace each edge case**: Mentally execute the function. Does it handle the case correctly?  
#### 3. **Check test coverage**: Is there a test for this edge case? Flag gaps.  
#### 4. **Check interactions**: Could function A's output break function B's assumptions?

#### - **What happens**: [Incorrect behavior]

####   
#### ## Document to Evaluate  
####   
#### **File**: .adversarial/inputs/ADV-0049-code-review-input.md  
####   
#### # Code Review: ADV-0049 — DK003 Chained-In Bugfix + Pattern Lint Tests  
####   
#### ## Task Summary  
####   
#### ADV-0049 is an upstream sync task that:  
#### 1. Fixes a bug in `check_dk003()` where chained `in` comparisons (`a in b in c`) incorrectly reused `node.left` for all comparisons instead of tracking the evolving left operand  
#### 2. Adds 44 tests for the pattern_lint module (DK001-DK004 rules) — previously untested  
####   
#### The fix introduces a `current_left` variable that advances through each comparator in the chain, ensuring `a in b in c` correctly checks `(a in b)` and `(b in c)` rather than `(a in b)` and `(a in c)`.  
####   
#### ## Key Files Changed  
####   
#### - `scripts/core/pattern_lint.py` — Bugfix: track `current_left` through DK003 comparison loop  
#### - `tests/test_pattern_lint.py` — New: 44 tests covering all 4 lint rules + integration tests  
####   
#### ## Diff  
####   
#### ```diff  
#### diff --git a/scripts/core/pattern_lint.py b/scripts/core/pattern_lint.py  
#### index 48aa80c..9ea571e 100644  
#### --- a/scripts/core/pattern_lint.py  
#### +++ b/scripts/core/pattern_lint.py  
#### @@ -218,29 +218,35 @@ def check_dk003(tree: ast.AST, source_lines: list[str], path: str) -> list[Viola  
####          if not isinstance(node, ast.Compare):  
####              continue  
####   
#### +        current_left = node.left  
####          for op, comparator in zip(node.ops, node.comparators, strict=False):  
####              if not isinstance(op, ast.In):  
#### +                current_left = comparator  
####                  continue  
####   
####              # Skip collection literals — set, list, tuple, dict on the right  
####              if isinstance(comparator, (ast.Set, ast.List, ast.Tuple, ast.Dict)):  
#### +                current_left = comparator  
####                  continue  
####              # Skip set/frozenset/list/dict/tuple constructor calls  
####              if isinstance(comparator, ast.Call):  
####                  func_name = _extract_name(comparator.func)  
####                  if func_name in {"set", "frozenset", "list", "dict", "tuple"}:  
#### +                    current_left = comparator  
####                      continue  
####   
#### -            left = node.left  
#### +            left = current_left  
####              left_name = _extract_name(left)  
####              right_name = _extract_name(comparator)  
####   
####              if not left_name or not right_name:  
#### +                current_left = comparator  
####                  continue  
####   
####              # Skip if right side looks like a collection variable  
####              right_lower = right_name.lower().split(".")[-1]  # last segment  
####              if any(right_lower.endswith(s) for s in collection_suffixes):  
#### +                current_left = comparator  
####                  continue  
####   
####              # Both sides must look like identifier variables  
#### @@ -248,12 +254,14 @@ def check_dk003(tree: ast.AST, source_lines: list[str], path: str) -> list[Viola  
####              right_is_id = any(hint in right_name.lower() for hint in identifier_hints)  
####   
####              if not (left_is_id and right_is_id):  
#### +                current_left = comparator  
####                  continue  
####   
####              line = source_lines[node.lineno - 1] if node.lineno <= len(source_lines) else ""  
####   
####              # Suppressed by '# substring:' comment

####                  )  
####              )

#### +            current_left = comparator  
#### +  
####      return violations  
#### ```  
####   
#### ```diff  
#### diff --git a/tests/test_pattern_lint.py b/tests/test_pattern_lint.py  
#### new file mode 100644  
#### index 0000000..d3fa8c7  
#### --- /dev/null  
#### +++ b/tests/test_pattern_lint.py  
#### @@ -0,0 +1,383 @@  
#### +"""Tests for scripts/pattern_lint.py — project-specific lint rules."""  
#### +# 44 tests across 5 test classes:  
#### +# - TestDK001 (7 tests): str.replace for extension removal  
#### +# - TestDK002 (12 tests): missing encoding= in file I/O  
#### +# - TestDK003 (12 tests): 'in' for identifier comparison (incl. chained-in)  
#### +# - TestDK004 (10 tests): bare except Exception with pass/empty body  
#### +# - TestIntegration (2 tests): multi-rule and clean-code scenarios  
#### +# Uses sys.path.insert to import from scripts/core/ (not a Python package)  
#### ```  
####   
#### ## Review Focus Areas  
####   
#### 1. **Bugfix correctness**: Does `current_left` advance correctly at every exit point in the loop?  
#### 2. **Test coverage**: Are chained-in edge cases adequately tested?  
#### 3. **Import approach**: `sys.path.insert` for scripts/core/ — acceptable for non-package code?  
#### 4. **No regressions**: All 44 tests pass, existing tests unaffected  
####  

## Findings

**[ROBUSTNESS]: Unnecessary `strict=False` in `zip` for AST node processing**
- **Location**: `scripts/core/pattern_lint.py:check_dk003`
- **Edge case**: `zip(node.ops, node.comparators, strict=False)`
- **What happens**: The `ast.Compare` node guarantees that `len(node.ops)` is equal to `len(node.comparators)`. Explicitly setting `strict=False` is redundant for well-formed ASTs. While not a correctness bug with valid Python, `strict=True` would offer better robustness against potentially malformed (non-standard) AST inputs by failing loudly if lengths differed, rather than silently truncating comparisons. The addition of `strict=False` implies a specific intent which is not fully explained and is not necessary for standard AST parsing. If the target Python environment is older than 3.10, this would also cause a `TypeError`.
- **Tested?**: No (this is a robustness/implementation detail, not a functional bug per se, hence unlikely to have a dedicated test, but could be implicitly covered if malformed AST tests existed).

**[TESTING]: Inadequate test coverage for mixed operator chains in DK003**
- **Location**: `scripts/core/pattern_lint.py:check_dk003`
- **Edge case**: Chained comparisons with mixed operators, e.g., `a == b in c` or `a in b != c in d`.
- **What happens**: The `current_left` variable correctly advances even when an operator is not `ast.In` (e.g., `==` or `!=`). However, the existing test summary only mentions "chained-in" scenarios. There's no explicit confirmation that combinations involving non-`in` operators in the chain are specifically tested to ensure `current_left` behaves as expected, and that `in` violations are correctly detected (or not detected) when surrounded by other operators.
- **Tested?**: No (not explicitly mentioned in the test summary; should be a dedicated test case).

**[TESTING]: Inadequate test coverage for `current_left` originating from a skipped comparison**
- **Location**: `scripts/core/pattern_lint.py:check_dk003`
- **Edge case**: A chained comparison where the first `in` comparison is explicitly skipped due to one of the `continue` conditions (e.g., non-identifier `left`, collection literal on `right`, suppression comment), but the `current_left` correctly advances, allowing a *subsequent* `in` comparison in the chain to be processed. Example: `1 in some_list in my_id_var` where `1 in some_list` is skipped, but `some_list in my_id_var` should be checked (assuming `some_list` is considered an identifier for `left_is_id` purposes).
- **What happens**: The `current_left` logic appears robust to these skips, but without explicit tests, there's a risk that a subtle interaction could cause a later check in the chain to be incorrectly evaluated or missed.
- **Tested?**: No (not explicitly mentioned in the test summary; should be a dedicated test case).

## Test Gap Summary

| Edge Case                                                       | Function      | Tested? | Risk        |
|:----------------------------------------------------------------|:--------------|:--------|:------------|
| Mixed operators in comparison chain (e.g., `a == b in c`)       | `check_dk003` | No      | Medium      |
| `current_left` originates from a skipped comparison             | `check_dk003` | No      | Low         |
| `zip` with `strict=False` on potentially malformed ASTs         | `check_dk003` | No      | Low/Robustness |

## Verdict

- **CONCERNS**: Untested edge cases or robustness gaps. The core bugfix logic for `current_left` appears correct and robust in its advancement. However, the explicit `strict=False` in `zip` is an unusual and potentially unnecessary addition that could mask issues with malformed ASTs, and specific test cases for mixed operator chains and skipped initial comparisons are not explicitly confirmed.

#### # Spec Compliance Input: ADV-0054  
####   
#### ## Task Spec  
####   
#### # ADV-0054: Fix review_implementation.sh Bugs  
####   
#### **Status**: In Progress  
#### **Priority**: High  
#### **Type**: Bug Fix  
#### **Estimated Effort**: 1-2 hours  
#### **Created**: 2026-03-15  
#### **Reported By**: RMM-0001 (research-method-matrix project)  
####   
#### ## Summary  
####   
#### The `adversarial review` command and its underlying `review_implementation.sh` script  
#### have multiple bugs that make the review phase non-functional for downstream projects.  
#### These were discovered during real usage in the research-method-matrix project (RMM-0001).  
####   
#### The bugs affect both the **template** (what `adversarial init` generates for new projects)  
#### and the **CLI wrapper** (the `adversarial review` subcommand). The `/check-spec` skill  
#### also references a non-existent CLI command.  
####   
#### ## Bug Details  
####   
#### ### Bug 1: `mkdir -p` comes after first write (CRASH)  
####   
#### **Files**: `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template` (lines 105-107),  
#### `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` (lines 50-52)  
####   
#### The script writes artifacts on lines 105-107:  
#### ```bash  
#### git diff > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-implementation.diff"  
#### git diff --stat > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-change-summary.txt"  
#### git status --short > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-file-status.txt"  
#### ```  
####   
#### But `mkdir -p "$ARTIFACTS_DIR"` doesn't appear until much later in the committed script  
#### (line 89). The template doesn't have `mkdir -p` at all.  
####   
#### **Fix**: Add `mkdir -p "$ARTIFACTS_DIR"` and `mkdir -p "$LOG_DIR"` immediately before  
#### the artifact capture block (before the first `git diff >` redirect).  
####   
#### ### Bug 2: `git diff` captures wrong changes (WRONG OUTPUT)  
####   
#### **Files**: Same as Bug 1  
####   
#### The script uses bare `git diff` which only captures **unstaged** changes. On a feature  
#### branch where work is committed or staged, this produces empty or misleading output.  
#### The RMM project saw only a task file deletion (from `./scripts/project start` move)  
#### instead of the 5 source files with actual implementation changes.  
####   
#### **Fix**: Replace bare `git diff` with branch-aware diff:  
####   
#### ```bash  
#### # Detect the default branch  
#### DEFAULT_BRANCH=$(git symbolic-ref refs/remotes/origin/HEAD 2>/dev/null | sed 's@^refs/remotes/origin/@@' || echo "main")  
####   
#### # Capture ALL changes on this branch (committed + staged + unstaged)  
#### git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD" > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-implementation.diff"  
#### git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD" --stat > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-change-summary.txt"  
#### ```  
####   
#### Also update the `--stat` line that computes `LINES_CHANGED` to use the same range.  
####   
#### Keep `git status --short` as-is (it shows current working tree state, which is useful context).  
####   
#### ### Bug 3: `adversarial review` doesn't pass file argument (BROKEN CLI)  
####   
#### **File**: `adversarial_workflow/cli.py` (lines 2111-2160, 3182)  
####   
#### The `review` subcommand is registered with no arguments:  
#### ```python  
#### subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")  
#### ```  
####   
#### And the `review()` function calls the script without forwarding any argument:  
#### ```python  
#### result = subprocess.run([script], timeout=180)  
#### ```  
####   
#### But the script **requires** a task file argument and exits with an error without one.  
####   
#### **Fix**:  
#### 1. Add an optional positional argument to the `review` subparser:  
####    ```python  
####    review_parser = subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")  
####    review_parser.add_argument("task_file", nargs="?", help="Task file path (optional)")  
####    ```  
#### 2. Update `review()` to accept and pass the argument:  
####    ```python  
####    def review(task_file: str | None = None) -> int:  
####    ```  
#### 3. Pass it to the script: `subprocess.run([script, task_file] if task_file else [script], ...)`  
#### 4. Update the call site to pass `args.task_file`  
####   
#### ### Bug 4: `/check-spec` skill references non-existent command (BROKEN SKILL)  
####   
#### **File**: `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` (line 34)  
####   
#### The skill instructs:  
#### ```bash  
#### adversarial spec-compliance-fast .adversarial/inputs/<TASK-ID>-spec-compliance-input.md  
#### ```  
####   
#### But `spec-compliance-fast` is not a CLI subcommand. The spec-compliance evaluator exists  
#### at `.adversarial/evaluators/custom/spec-compliance.yml` and should be invoked via:  
#### ```bash  
#### adversarial evaluate .adversarial/inputs/<TASK-ID>-spec-compliance-input.md --evaluator spec-compliance  
#### ```  
####   
#### **Fix**: Update `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` Step 3 to use the correct command.  
####   
#### ## Acceptance Criteria  
####   
#### - [ ] **Bug 1**: `mkdir -p` for artifacts and log dirs happens before first file write in both template and committed script  
#### - [ ] **Bug 2**: Diff captures all branch changes via `git diff <default-branch>...HEAD`, not bare `git diff`  
#### - [ ] **Bug 3**: `adversarial review <task-file>` passes the file argument through to the script

####

#### 4. `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` — Bug 4  
####   
#### ## Notes  
####   
#### - **Issue 5 from RMM report** (aider skipping gitignored artifacts) is already fixed — both the template and committed script have `--no-gitignore`. The RMM project likely had an older copy.  
#### - The committed `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` is a local copy that diverges slightly from the template. Consider whether to keep both in sync or remove the committed copy.  
#### - `config.yml` in this repo is missing `artifacts_directory` — the script falls back to parsing it from config, which returns empty. This doesn't crash because `init` creates the dir, but the path variable will be empty for repos that don't set it. The template handles this via config parsing. Not in scope for this task but worth noting.

#### +# ADV-0054: Fix review_implementation.sh Bugs  
#### +  
#### +**Status**: In Progress  
#### +**Priority**: High  
#### +**Type**: Bug Fix  
#### +**Estimated Effort**: 1-2 hours  
#### +**Created**: 2026-03-15  
#### +**Reported By**: RMM-0001 (research-method-matrix project)  
#### +  
#### +## Summary  
#### +  
#### +The `adversarial review` command and its underlying `review_implementation.sh` script  
#### +have multiple bugs that make the review phase non-functional for downstream projects.  
#### +These were discovered during real usage in the research-method-matrix project (RMM-0001).  
#### +  
#### +The bugs affect both the **template** (what `adversarial init` generates for new projects)  
#### +and the **CLI wrapper** (the `adversarial review` subcommand). The `/check-spec` skill  
#### +also references a non-existent CLI command.  
#### +  
#### +## Bug Details  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 1: `mkdir -p` comes after first write (CRASH)  
#### +  
#### +**Files**: `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template` (lines 105-107),  
#### +`.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` (lines 50-52)  
#### +  
#### +The script writes artifacts on lines 105-107:  
#### +```bash  
#### +git diff > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-implementation.diff"  
#### +git diff --stat > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-change-summary.txt"  
#### +git status --short > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-file-status.txt"  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +But `mkdir -p "$ARTIFACTS_DIR"` doesn't appear until much later in the committed script  
#### +(line 89). The template doesn't have `mkdir -p` at all.  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**: Add `mkdir -p "$ARTIFACTS_DIR"` and `mkdir -p "$LOG_DIR"` immediately before  
#### +the artifact capture block (before the first `git diff >` redirect).  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 2: `git diff` captures wrong changes (WRONG OUTPUT)  
#### +  
#### +**Files**: Same as Bug 1  
#### +  
#### +The script uses bare `git diff` which only captures **unstaged** changes. On a feature  
#### +branch where work is committed or staged, this produces empty or misleading output.  
#### +The RMM project saw only a task file deletion (from `./scripts/project start` move)  
#### +instead of the 5 source files with actual implementation changes.  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**: Replace bare `git diff` with branch-aware diff:  
#### +  
#### +```bash  
#### +# Detect the default branch  
#### +DEFAULT_BRANCH=$(git symbolic-ref refs/remotes/origin/HEAD 2>/dev/null | sed 's@^refs/remotes/origin/@@' || echo "main")  
#### +  
#### +# Capture ALL changes on this branch (committed + staged + unstaged)  
#### +git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD" > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-implementation.diff"  
#### +git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD" --stat > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-change-summary.txt"  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +Also update the `--stat` line that computes `LINES_CHANGED` to use the same range.  
#### +  
#### +Keep `git status --short` as-is (it shows current working tree state, which is useful context).  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 3: `adversarial review` doesn't pass file argument (BROKEN CLI)  
#### +  
#### +**File**: `adversarial_workflow/cli.py` (lines 2111-2160, 3182)  
#### +  
#### +The `review` subcommand is registered with no arguments:  
#### +```python  
#### +subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +And the `review()` function calls the script without forwarding any argument:  
#### +```python  
#### +result = subprocess.run([script], timeout=180)  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +But the script **requires** a task file argument and exits with an error without one.  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**:  
#### +1. Add an optional positional argument to the `review` subparser:  
#### +   ```python  
#### +   review_parser = subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")  
#### +   review_parser.add_argument("task_file", nargs="?", help="Task file path (optional)")  
#### +   ```  
#### +2. Update `review()` to accept and pass the argument:  
#### +   ```python  
#### +   def review(task_file: str | None = None) -> int:  
#### +   ```  
#### +3. Pass it to the script: `subprocess.run([script, task_file] if task_file else [script], ...)`  
#### +4. Update the call site to pass `args.task_file`  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 4: `/check-spec` skill references non-existent command (BROKEN SKILL)  
#### +  
#### +**File**: `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` (line 34)  
#### +  
#### +The skill instructs:  
#### +```bash  
#### +adversarial spec-compliance-fast .adversarial/inputs/<TASK-ID>-spec-compliance-input.md  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +But `spec-compliance-fast` is not a CLI subcommand. The spec-compliance evaluator exists  
#### +at `.adversarial/evaluators/custom/spec-compliance.yml` and should be invoked via:  
#### +```bash  
#### +adversarial evaluate .adversarial/inputs/<TASK-ID>-spec-compliance-input.md --evaluator spec-compliance  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**: Update `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` Step 3 to use the correct command.  
#### +  
#### +## Acceptance Criteria  
#### +  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 1**: `mkdir -p` for artifacts and log dirs happens before first file write in both template and committed script  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 2**: Diff captures all branch changes via `git diff <default-branch>...HEAD`, not bare `git diff`  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 3**: `adversarial review <task-file>` passes the file argument through to the script  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 4**: `/check-spec` skill references correct `adversarial evaluate` command  
#### +- [ ] **Tests**: Existing tests still pass (`pytest tests/ -v`)  
#### +- [ ] **Consistency**: Template and committed script remain in sync (or committed script is removed if redundant)  
#### +  
#### +## Files to Modify  
#### +  
#### +1. `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template` — Bugs 1, 2  
#### +2. `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` — Bugs 1, 2 (keep in sync with template)  
#### +3. `adversarial_workflow/cli.py` — Bug 3 (review subparser + review() function + call site)  
#### +4. `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` — Bug 4  
#### +  
#### +## Notes  
#### +  
#### +- **Issue 5 from RMM report** (aider skipping gitignored artifacts) is already fixed — both the template and committed script have `--no-gitignore`. The RMM project likely had an older copy.  
#### +- The committed `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` is a local copy that diverges slightly from the template. Consider whether to keep both in sync or remove the committed copy.  
#### +- `config.yml` in this repo is missing `artifacts_directory` — the script falls back to parsing it from config, which returns empty. This doesn't crash because `init` creates the dir, but the path variable will be empty for repos that don't set it. The template handles this via config parsing. Not in scope for this task but worth noting.

### Spec Drift

**[ADDITION]: Capture staged and uncommitted changes explicitly**
- **Spec says**: "Capture ALL changes on this branch (committed + staged + unstaged) `git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD"`"
- **Code does**: In addition to `git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD"`, the scripts (`review_implementation.sh` and its template) explicitly capture `git diff --cached` (staged) and `git diff` (unstaged) changes separately, appending them to the diff and summary files with headers.
- **Impact**: This is a beneficial enhancement, providing more granular details about changes, which aligns with the spirit of capturing "ALL changes" without contradicting the spec. OK.

**[DEVIATION]: `adversarial review` `task_file` argument is required, not optional**
- **Spec says**: "Add an *optional* positional argument to the `review` subparser: `review_parser.add_argument("task_file", nargs="?", help="Task file path (optional)")`"
- **Code does**: The implementation adds `review_parser.add_argument("task_file", help="Task file path")`, making the `task_file` argument required. The `subprocess.run` call also directly uses `task_file` without handling its potential absence.
- **Impact**: This deviates from the specified optionality. Users *must* provide a task file, whereas the spec indicated it should be optional. This is a functional regression from the spec. PROBLEM.

### Gaps

1.  **Missing Test Coverage for Bug Fixes**: The acceptance criteria mention that "Existing tests still pass". However, the provided `git diff` does not include any new or modified tests specifically designed to verify that Bug 1, Bug 2, Bug 3, and Bug 4 are actually fixed. For instance, there are no tests to confirm directory creation order, correct diff output under various git states, correct argument passing for the `review` command, or the `check-spec` skill's command execution. This leaves the new/corrected behaviors untested.
2.  **CLI Argument Optionality**: The `task_file` argument for `adversarial review` was specified as optional (`nargs="?"`) in the fix description but implemented as a required argument in `adversarial_workflow/cli.py`. This is a functional gap where the CLI's behavior does not match the specification for flexibility.

### Verdict

-   **MOSTLY_COMPLIANT**: The core logic for Bug 1, Bug 2, and Bug 4 is implemented correctly according to the spec. Bug 3's primary goal of passing the task file argument is met, but the argument's specified optionality was missed, making it required. The most significant concern is the complete lack of specific test coverage for these bug fixes, which makes verifying the fixes and preventing regressions difficult.

#### +        and unstaged_diff.returncode == 0

#### +# ADV-0054: Fix review_implementation.sh Bugs  
#### +  
#### +**Status**: In Progress  
#### +**Priority**: High  
#### +**Type**: Bug Fix  
#### +**Estimated Effort**: 1-2 hours  
#### +**Created**: 2026-03-15  
#### +**Reported By**: RMM-0001 (research-method-matrix project)  
#### +  
#### +## Summary  
#### +  
#### +The `adversarial review` command and its underlying `review_implementation.sh` script  
#### +have multiple bugs that make the review phase non-functional for downstream projects.  
#### +These were discovered during real usage in the research-method-matrix project (RMM-0001).  
#### +  
#### +The bugs affect both the **template** (what `adversarial init` generates for new projects)  
#### +and the **CLI wrapper** (the `adversarial review` subcommand). The `/check-spec` skill  
#### +also references a non-existent CLI command.  
#### +  
#### +## Bug Details  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 1: `mkdir -p` comes after first write (CRASH)  
#### +  
#### +**Files**: `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template` (lines 105-107),  
#### +`.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` (lines 50-52)  
#### +  
#### +The script writes artifacts on lines 105-107:  
#### +```bash  
#### +git diff > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-implementation.diff"  
#### +git diff --stat > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-change-summary.txt"  
#### +git status --short > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-file-status.txt"  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +But `mkdir -p "$ARTIFACTS_DIR"` doesn't appear until much later in the committed script  
#### +(line 89). The template doesn't have `mkdir -p` at all.  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**: Add `mkdir -p "$ARTIFACTS_DIR"` and `mkdir -p "$LOG_DIR"` immediately before  
#### +the artifact capture block (before the first `git diff >` redirect).  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 2: `git diff` captures wrong changes (WRONG OUTPUT)  
#### +  
#### +**Files**: Same as Bug 1  
#### +  
#### +The script uses bare `git diff` which only captures **unstaged** changes. On a feature  
#### +branch where work is committed or staged, this produces empty or misleading output.  
#### +The RMM project saw only a task file deletion (from `./scripts/project start` move)  
#### +instead of the 5 source files with actual implementation changes.  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**: Replace bare `git diff` with branch-aware diff:  
#### +  
#### +```bash  
#### +# Detect the default branch  
#### +DEFAULT_BRANCH=$(git symbolic-ref refs/remotes/origin/HEAD 2>/dev/null | sed 's@^refs/remotes/origin/@@' || echo "main")  
#### +  
#### +# Capture ALL changes on this branch (committed + staged + unstaged)  
#### +git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD" > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-implementation.diff"  
#### +git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD" --stat > "${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-change-summary.txt"  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +Also update the `--stat` line that computes `LINES_CHANGED` to use the same range.  
#### +  
#### +Keep `git status --short` as-is (it shows current working tree state, which is useful context).  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 3: `adversarial review` doesn't pass file argument (BROKEN CLI)  
#### +  
#### +**File**: `adversarial_workflow/cli.py` (lines 2111-2160, 3182)  
#### +  
#### +The `review` subcommand is registered with no arguments:  
#### +```python  
#### +subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +And the `review()` function calls the script without forwarding any argument:  
#### +```python  
#### +result = subprocess.run([script], timeout=180)  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +But the script **requires** a task file argument and exits with an error without one.  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**:  
#### +1. Add an optional positional argument to the `review` subparser:  
#### +   ```python  
#### +   review_parser = subparsers.add_parser("review", help="Run Phase 3: Code review")  
#### +   review_parser.add_argument("task_file", nargs="?", help="Task file path (optional)")  
#### +   ```  
#### +2. Update `review()` to accept and pass the argument:  
#### +   ```python  
#### +   def review(task_file: str | None = None) -> int:  
#### +   ```  
#### +3. Pass it to the script: `subprocess.run([script, task_file] if task_file else [script], ...)`  
#### +4. Update the call site to pass `args.task_file`  
#### +  
#### +### Bug 4: `/check-spec` skill references non-existent command (BROKEN SKILL)  
#### +  
#### +**File**: `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` (line 34)  
#### +  
#### +The skill instructs:  
#### +```bash  
#### +adversarial spec-compliance-fast .adversarial/inputs/<TASK-ID>-spec-compliance-input.md  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +But `spec-compliance-fast` is not a CLI subcommand. The spec-compliance evaluator exists  
#### +at `.adversarial/evaluators/custom/spec-compliance.yml` and should be invoked via:  
#### +```bash  
#### +adversarial evaluate .adversarial/inputs/<TASK-ID>-spec-compliance-input.md --evaluator spec-compliance  
#### +```  
#### +  
#### +**Fix**: Update `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` Step 3 to use the correct command.  
#### +  
#### +## Acceptance Criteria  
#### +  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 1**: `mkdir -p` for artifacts and log dirs happens before first file write in both template and committed script  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 2**: Diff captures all branch changes via `git diff <default-branch>...HEAD`, not bare `git diff`  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 3**: `adversarial review <task-file>` passes the file argument through to the script  
#### +- [ ] **Bug 4**: `/check-spec` skill references correct `adversarial evaluate` command  
#### +- [ ] **Tests**: Existing tests still pass (`pytest tests/ -v`)  
#### +- [ ] **Consistency**: Template and committed script remain in sync (or committed script is removed if redundant)  
#### +  
#### +## Files to Modify  
#### +  
#### +1. `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template` — Bugs 1, 2  
#### +2. `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` — Bugs 1, 2 (keep in sync with template)  
#### +3. `adversarial_workflow/cli.py` — Bug 3 (review subparser + review() function + call site)  
#### +4. `.claude/commands/check-spec.md` — Bug 4  
#### +  
#### +## Notes  
#### +  
#### +- **Issue 5 from RMM report** (aider skipping gitignored artifacts) is already fixed — both the template and committed script have `--no-gitignore`. The RMM project likely had an older copy.  
#### +- The committed `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` is a local copy that diverges slightly from the template. Consider whether to keep both in sync or remove the committed copy.  
#### +- `config.yml` in this repo is missing `artifacts_directory` — the script falls back to parsing it from config, which returns empty. This doesn't crash because `init` creates the dir, but the path variable will be empty for repos that don't set it. The template handles this via config parsing. Not in scope for this task but worth noting.  
#### ```  
####  

### Findings

**ROBUSTNESS**: Empty `ARTIFACTS_DIR` or `LOG_DIR` in bash script
- **Location**: `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` and `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template`
- **Edge case**: `ARTIFACTS_DIR` or `LOG_DIR` environment variables are unset or empty strings when the script executes.
- **What happens**: `mkdir -p ""` might create a directory in the current working directory, or `mkdir -p "/invalid/path"` would fail (if the parent path is not writable). In either case, subsequent `git diff >` commands attempting to write to `"${ARTIFACTS_DIR}${TASK_NUM}-implementation.diff"` would either fail (if `ARTIFACTS_DIR` led to an invalid path) or write to an unexpected location, potentially leading to empty or missing artifact files without clear error reporting, causing the review process to be incomplete or misleading. The script does not explicitly check the success of `mkdir -p` or the validity of these paths.
- **Tested?**: No (explicitly noted as "not feasible without mocking git/filesystem").

**ROBUSTNESS**: Default branch detection in bash script can lead to crashes if `main` does not exist.
- **Location**: `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` and `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template`
- **Edge case**: `git symbolic-ref --short refs/remotes/origin/HEAD` fails (e.g., no `origin` remote, or `origin/HEAD` not set), causing `DEFAULT_BRANCH` to fallback to `main` (via `${DEFAULT_BRANCH:-main}`), but the `main` branch itself does not exist in the repository (e.g., a new repository or one using `master` as its primary branch).
- **What happens**: `git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD"` would execute as `git diff main...HEAD`. If `main` does not exist as a ref, this command will fail with a `fatal: bad revision 'main...'` error, causing the `review_implementation.sh` script to crash. While `cli.py`'s pre-check attempts to prevent this, the bash script still has this vulnerability.
- **Tested?**: No (explicitly noted as "not feasible without mocking git/filesystem").

**ROBUSTNESS**: `cli.py`'s `review()` pre-check can mask underlying `git` errors and lead to script crashes.
- **Location**: `adversarial_workflow/cli.py:review`
- **Edge case**: The `base` branch (derived from `default_branch` or defaulting to `main`) or the `HEAD` reference itself is invalid for `git diff` operations (e.g., `main` branch does not exist, or the repository is in an "unborn branch" state with no commits).
- **What happens**: `subprocess.run(["git", "diff", "--quiet", f"{base}...HEAD"], ...)` (for `branch_diff`) will return a non-zero exit code if the `git diff` command fails due to invalid revisions. This correctly prevents the "No git changes detected!" warning in `cli.py`. However, `cli.py` then proceeds to execute the `review_implementation.sh` script. The bash script will then attempt `git diff "${DEFAULT_BRANCH}...HEAD"` which will also fail, causing the bash script to crash. This means `cli.py` doesn't provide a more informative error message about the invalid Git state to the user, leading to a less graceful failure.
- **Tested?**: No (unit tests likely don't mock these specific `git` error scenarios).

**ROBUSTNESS**: `review_implementation.sh` handles non-existent or empty `task_file` arguments poorly.
- **Location**: `.adversarial/scripts/review_implementation.sh` and `adversarial_workflow/templates/review_implementation.sh.template`
- **Edge case**: The `task_file` argument passed to the bash script (e.g., from `cli.py`) is a path to a non-existent file, a directory, or an empty string (`""`).
- **What happens**:
    *   If `task_file` is non-existent or a directory: `TASK_NUM=$(basename "$TASK_FILE" .md)` will still extract a name (e.g., `nonexistent` or `mydir`). Artifact files will be created using this (potentially misleading) name (e.g., `nonexistent-implementation.diff`). The script does not validate the existence or type of `TASK_FILE`, which could lead to confusion in the generated artifacts.
    *   If `task_file` is an empty string: `TASK_NUM=$(basename "" .md)` would result in `TASK_NUM` being `.` (current directory). This would lead to artifact files like `./-implementation.diff` being created in `$ARTIFACTS_DIR`, potentially overwriting generic artifacts from other runs or being highly confusing.
- **Tested?**: No (explicitly noted as "not feasible without mocking git/filesystem").

### Test Gap Summary

| Edge Case | Function/File | Tested? | Risk |
|-----------------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------|---------|--------|
| Empty `ARTIFACTS_DIR`/`LOG_DIR`               | `review_implementation.sh`                            | No      | High   |
| Non-existent `main` branch (fallback)         | `review_implementation.sh`                            | No      | High   |
| `cli.py` pre-check with invalid `git` refs    | `adversarial_workflow/cli.py:review`                  | No      | Medium |
| Non-existent/malformed `task_file` (bash)     | `review_implementation.sh`                            | No      | High   |
| `origin/HEAD` not configured, `master` default | `review_implementation.sh`                            | No      | Medium |

### Verdict

**CONCERNS**: While the stated bugs are fixed, several robustness gaps and untested edge cases persist in the shell scripts and their interaction with the Python CLI. Specifically, issues around non-existent default branches, invalid `task_file` arguments, and empty environment variables for artifact directories could lead to script crashes or misleading results. The `cli.py` wrapper, while improved, could offer more specific error handling for underlying `git` command failures rather than just allowing the bash script to crash.

## Concerns & Risks
- [CRITICAL] The plan does not specify how to handle potential errors or failures in the new linting steps, which could block CI unnecessarily.
- [MEDIUM] The plan assumes that the changes to `ci-check.sh` (ADV-0058) will be completed and aligned, but does not specify a fallback if this dependency is delayed.
- [LOW] The plan does not address potential performance impacts of running additional linting steps in CI, which could increase build times.

## Missing or Unclear
- The plan does not specify how to handle errors or failures in the new linting steps.
- It lacks a detailed explanation of how the changes will be tested to ensure they do not introduce regressions.
- There is no mention of updating documentation to reflect the new CI processes and requirements.

## Specific Recommendations
1. Include error handling strategies for the new linting steps to prevent CI from being blocked by non-critical issues.
2. Consider adding a section on testing the changes to ensure they do not introduce regressions or performance issues.
3. Update the plan to include documentation changes that reflect the new CI processes and requirements.

## Questions for Plan Author
1. How will errors in the new linting steps be handled to prevent unnecessary CI failures?
2. What testing will be conducted to ensure the changes do not introduce regressions or performance issues?
3. Are there any plans to update documentation to reflect the new CI processes and requirements?

- Provide a plan for testing the changes to ensure they do not introduce regressions or performance issues.

#### # Code Review Input: ADV-0058 — Fix ci-check.sh / GitHub Actions Parity  
####   
#### **PR**: https://github.com/movito/adversarial-workflow/pull/50  
#### **Branch**: `feature/ADV-0058-fix-ci-check-parity`  
#### **Commits**: 3  
####   
#### ## What Changed  
####   
#### ci-check.sh claimed to "mirror GitHub Actions" but disagreed on coverage thresholds,  
#### lint scope, and produced false failures every run. Flagged in 4 of 6 retros. Also fixes  
#### a permission gap that blocked agents from using `SKIP_TESTS=1 git commit`.  
####   
#### ### `scripts/core/ci-check.sh`  
#### - Removed `--cov-fail-under=80` (GitHub Actions doesn't enforce it; Codecov gates coverage)  
#### - Changed pattern lint scope from `scripts/ tests/` to `adversarial_workflow/` (matches pre-commit)  
#### - Fixed unquoted `$PY_FILES` with `find -print0 | xargs -0`  
#### - Made pattern lint advisory (non-blocking) — 34 pre-existing DK002 violations tracked in ADV-0061  
#### - Added directory existence guard for `adversarial_workflow/`  
#### - Updated header comment to accurately describe checks  
####   
#### ### `.claude/settings.json`  
#### - Added `Bash(SKIP_TESTS=1 git *)` to allow list (scoped to git only per BugBot review)  
####   
#### ### `delegation/tasks/1-backlog/ADV-0061-fix-dk002-adversarial-workflow.md` (new)  
#### - Backlog task to fix 34 DK002 violations and promote pattern lint back to blocking  
####   
#### ## Key Design Decision  
####   
#### Pattern lint is **advisory** (warn, not fail) because:  
#### 1. GitHub Actions doesn't run pattern lint at all  
#### 2. Pre-commit gates it for staged files  
#### 3. 34 pre-existing violations would cause false failures  
#### 4. ADV-0061 tracks the cleanup; once done, lint becomes blocking again  
####

I've analyzed the changes in `scripts/core/ci-check.sh` concerning the pattern lint and test suite sections, and the update to `.claude/settings.json`. The fixes to `ci-check.sh`, such as using `find -print0 | xargs -0` and adding a directory existence guard, significantly improve its robustness. The pattern lint is now advisory, and test coverage thresholds are delegated to Codecov, which aligns with the stated goals. The `.claude/settings.json` change adds a specific permission for `SKIP_TESTS=1 git *` commands, which appears correctly scoped.

#### # ADV-0057: Review Script Robustness Improvements  
####   
#### **Status**: In Progress  
#### **Priority**: Medium  
#### **Type**: Enhancement  
#### **Estimated Effort**: 1-2 hours  
#### **Created**: 2026-03-15  
#### **Updated**: 2026-03-19  
#### **Origin**: ADV-0054 code-reviewer-fast evaluator findings  
####   
#### ## Summary  
####   
#### The adversarial code-review evaluator (Gemini Flash) identified 4 robustness  
#### gaps in `review_implementation.sh` and its CLI wrapper during the ADV-0054  
#### review. All are pre-existing edge cases (not regressions), but worth hardening.  
####   
#### ## Issues to Address  
####   
#### ### 1. Empty `ARTIFACTS_DIR` / `LOG_DIR` from config parsing  
####   
#### **Risk**: Medium  
#### **Files**: `review_implementation.sh`, template  
####   
#### If `artifacts_directory` or `log_directory` is missing from `.adversarial/config.yml`,  
#### the variables are empty strings. `mkdir -p ""` creates nothing useful, and subsequent  
#### file writes go to unexpected paths.  
####   
#### **Fix**: Add validation after config parsing:  
#### ```bash  
#### ARTIFACTS_DIR=${ARTIFACTS_DIR:-.adversarial/artifacts/}  
#### LOG_DIR=${LOG_DIR:-.adversarial/logs/}  
#### ```  
####   
#### ### 2. Non-existent default branch fallback  
####   
#### **Risk**: Low  
#### **Files**: `review_implementation.sh`, template, `cli.py`  
####   
#### If `origin/HEAD` is not set AND the repo uses `master` (not `main`), the fallback  
#### to `main` causes `git diff main...HEAD` to fail.  
####   
#### **Fix**: After setting `DEFAULT_BRANCH`, verify the ref exists:  
#### ```bash  
#### if ! git rev-parse --verify "$DEFAULT_BRANCH" >/dev/null 2>&1; then  
####   echo "Error: Cannot find base branch '$DEFAULT_BRANCH'. Set origin/HEAD or pass branch explicitly."  
####   exit 1  
#### fi  
#### ```  
####   
#### ### 3. CLI pre-check error handling  
####   
#### **Risk**: Low  
#### **Files**: `adversarial_workflow/cli.py` (`review()`)  
####   
#### When `git diff base...HEAD` fails due to invalid refs, the non-zero exit code  
#### correctly prevents the "no changes" abort, but the script then crashes with an  
#### unhelpful git error. The CLI could catch this and provide a better message.  
####   
#### **Fix**: Check `branch_diff.returncode` for values > 1 (git error vs changes detected)  
#### and report the issue before invoking the script.  
####   
#### ### 4. Invalid `task_file` edge cases in bash script  
####   
#### **Risk**: Low  
#### **Files**: `review_implementation.sh`, template  
####   
#### The script validates file existence but doesn't handle empty strings well  
#### (`basename "" .md` produces `.`). The CLI now requires `task_file`, so this  
#### is only reachable if the script is invoked directly.  
####   
#### **Fix**: Add early validation:  
#### ```bash  
#### if [ -z "$TASK_FILE" ] || [ ! -f "$TASK_FILE" ]; then  
####   echo "Error: Task file not found or not specified: $TASK_FILE"  
####   exit 1  
#### fi  
#### ```  
####   
#### ## Acceptance Criteria  
####   
#### - [ ] Config variables have sensible defaults when missing from config.yml  
#### - [ ] Default branch fallback validates the ref exists before using it  
#### - [ ] CLI provides clear error when git state is invalid for review  
#### - [ ] Script handles empty/invalid task_file gracefully  
#### - [ ] Template and committed script remain in sync  
#### - [ ] All existing tests pass  
####   
#### ## Notes  
####   
#### - These are all pre-existing issues, not regressions from ADV-0054

#### You are an adversarial code reviewer. Your job is NOT to verify that code meets acceptance  
#### criteria — that's already been done. Your job is to find bugs. Specifically: edge cases,  
#### boundary conditions, incorrect assumptions, and logic errors that a checklist-based review  
#### would miss.  
####   
#### Think like a fuzzer, not like a manager. For every function, ask: "How could this break?"  
####   
#### {content}  
####   
#### ## Review Protocol  
####   
#### ### Phase 1: Identify Attack Surface  
####   
#### For each function in the changed code:  
#### 1. List all inputs (parameters, file reads, environment, global state)  
#### 2. For each input, enumerate boundary values:  
####    - Empty/zero/null  
####    - Single element vs many  
####    - Strings that are prefixes of other strings  
####    - Paths that don't exist or have no permissions  
####    - Collections with duplicates or cycles  
####    - Values at type boundaries (max int, empty dict, single-char string)  
#### 3. Identify implicit assumptions the code makes about its inputs  
####   
#### ### Phase 2: Trace Execution Paths  
####   
#### For each boundary value identified above:  
#### 1. Mentally execute the function with that input  
#### 2. Track what happens at each branch, loop, and operation  
#### 3. Flag any path where:  
####    - A string operation could produce an empty string unexpectedly  
####    - A collection could be empty when iterated  
####    - A file/path could not exist  
####    - An index could be out of bounds  
####    - A division could be by zero  
####    - A type assumption could be violated  
####    - A prefix/suffix check could match unintended values  
####   
#### ### Phase 3: Cross-Reference Tests  
####   
#### For each edge case identified in Phases 1-2:  
#### 1. Check if the test file contains a test for this specific case  
#### 2. If tested: note it as covered  
#### 3. If NOT tested: flag it as a test gap, even if the code handles it correctly  
#### 4. If the code does NOT handle it correctly: flag as a bug  
####   
#### ### Phase 4: Assess Interactions  
####   
#### Look beyond individual functions:  
#### 1. Do any functions share mutable state that could cause race conditions?  
#### 2. Could the order of operations matter (e.g., file written before check)?  
#### 3. Are there assumptions about data format that could be violated by upstream changes?  
#### 4. Could error handling in one function mask errors in another?  
####   
#### ## Output Format  
####   
#### ### Summary  
#### [2-3 sentences: what was reviewed, overall assessment, number of findings by severity]  
####   
#### ### Findings  
####   
#### For each finding:  
####   
#### **[CORRECTNESS/ROBUSTNESS/TESTING/INTERACTION]: [Title]**  
#### - **Location**: `file.py:function_name` (line N)  
#### - **Edge case**: [The specific input or condition that triggers the issue]  
#### - **What happens**: [Concrete description of incorrect behavior]  
#### - **Expected**: [What should happen instead]  
#### - **Test coverage**: Covered / NOT covered  
#### - **Severity**: Bug (broken now) / Latent (breaks under specific conditions) / Gap (untested path)  
####   
#### ### Edge Cases Verified Clean  
#### [List edge cases you checked that ARE handled correctly — shows your work]  
####   
#### ### Test Gap Summary  
#### | Edge Case | Function | Tested? | Risk |  
#### |-----------|----------|---------|------|  
#### [Table of all identified edge cases and their test coverage status]  
####   
#### ### Verdict  
####   
#### - **PASS**: No correctness bugs found. Edge cases handled. Test coverage adequate.  
#### - **CONCERNS**: No confirmed bugs, but untested edge cases or robustness gaps that should be addressed.  
#### - **FAIL**: One or more correctness bugs found. Must fix before merge.  
####   
#### For CONCERNS and FAIL, list the specific findings that drove the verdict.  
####   
####
